However, Hongchangshun, a store opened by Zhang Tingxian, a member of the executive committee of the Chamber of Commerce, refused the inspection and closed its doors. Its person in charge was handed over to the Public Security Bureau by the students to be guarded, pending a decision by the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for punishment. (30th Special Dispatch)

Grand Review of Student Volunteer Army in Tianjin

(Tianjin) The Municipal Government, based on a protest from the Japanese consulate on the 29th, forwarded a letter to the Municipal Party Headquarters, requesting that the grand review of the student volunteer army be stopped. The Student National Salvation United Association convened an emergency meeting on the evening of the 29th, stating that the students' organization of the volunteer army was for physical training and strengthening the country's foundation, and that the Japanese consulate should not interfere. It was decided that the review would be held on the morning of the 30th. If anyone tried to stop it, the students would sacrifice themselves against the machine guns. However, fearing incidents, parents forbade their children from going to school, so only over a thousand people attended the exercises on the morning of the 30th. They were reviewed by Wang Jixu, the president of the Engineering College, and their spirit and discipline were excellent. (30th Special Dispatch)

Proposals for Party and Government Reform Drafted by Guangdong

The Central Government Believes They Violate the Party Constitution

Should Not Be Discussed at This Time

(Nanjing) According to the Central News Agency, on the morning of the 28th, the Guangdong representatives submitted a proposal for party and government reform before the meeting. Cai Yuanpei and others considered this matter to be of great importance and did not allow it to be discussed. The original proposal was telegraphed to the Central Government. The Central Government replied in a telegram, stating, in essence, that regardless of the content of the proposal for party and government reform, its spirit was not in line with the main purpose of uniting against foreign aggression. At this time, for the sake of the party and the country, the only thing to do is to gather in the capital and jointly overcome the national crisis. As for the fundamental issues of party and government, they should be discussed and resolved by a majority of the party. There is no reason to decide on major national plans for the whole party and the whole country through discussions by a dozen people in Shanghai. Since people are already party members, they must abide by the party constitution together. As fellow citizens, they should respond to the national crisis. If loving the party and saving the country comes from sincerity and is not for the purpose of dividing up power and wealth as rumored outside, such proposals that violate the party constitution and disregard the national crisis should not be put forward for discussion, so as not to betray the hopes of the people. The proposals drafted by Guangdong are recorded below:

Proposals for Party and Government Reform drafted by Guangdong: (1) Regarding the unified conference and the conference of the unified government: A. Organization: This conference will be jointly organized by the Central Executive and Supervisory Committee's extraordinary meeting and five representatives from each of the Nanjing Central Government. B. Tasks: 1. To decide on the establishment of a unified government; 2. To discuss the process of the unified party affairs conference. C. Schedule: To be decided by the representatives of both sides. 2. Conference on unifying party affairs: A. Organization: To be jointly organized by the Central Executive and Supervisory Committee members of the first, second, and third sessions of the party. B. Tasks: To discuss everything about convening the Fourth National Congress of the party; 2. To discuss the unification of the two central organs of Guangdong and Nanjing. C. Schedule: To be held immediately after the conclusion of the unified government conference. (2) Regarding political matters: 1. The Chairman of the National Government is the head of state and does not bear actual administrative responsibility, similar to the president of a cabinet system country, with a term of three years. 2. The President of the Executive Yuan bears actual administrative responsibility, similar to the prime minister of a cabinet system country. 3. The presidents of the Legislative, Judicial, Examination, and Supervisory Yuans do not advance or retreat with the President of the Executive Yuan. 4. The Chairman of the National Government and the presidents of the various Yuans shall not be filled by active-duty military personnel. 5. The functions and powers of the members of the National Government are to handle conflicts of jurisdiction between the various Yuans. 6. The Chairman of the National Government is elected by a vote of the Central Executive Committee. 7. The President of the Executive Yuan is proposed by the Chairman to the Central Committee for approval. (3) Regarding the military and political system: 1. The National Government shall establish a National Defense Committee, with a number of members appointed by the National Government and designating 3 to 7 standing committee members. 2. The National Defense Committee does not directly issue orders. All military orders are issued by the National Government. 3. A number of national defense zones shall be established in the border areas, with a national defense branch in each zone. The division of national defense zones shall not be the same as the existing provinces and regions. 4. Civilians must be included as members of the National Defense Committee and its branches. 5. Provinces in the interior that are not related to national defense shall not station many troops in peacetime. Local security shall be maintained by military police. 6. To determine the military establishment, with the division as the largest unit. 7. To transfer the existing excess troops to the border areas for land reclamation. 8. The National Government shall still establish a Ministry of Military Administration and a General Staff Headquarters. The suppression of bandits shall be temporarily commanded by a commander-in-chief for bandit suppression. 9. A separate department shall be established for military supplies. (4) Regarding finance: A. Principles: 1. To achieve financial transparency; 2. To strictly implement the budget system. B. Measures: 1. To establish a special Financial Committee, with the government granting the following powers: A. To reorganize finances; B. To implement the budget; C. To audit and reconcile accounts; D. To publicize income and expenditure accounts. 2. The Financial Committee shall be organized with 15 members, 3 from the government, 3 from the banking industry, 3 from commerce, 3 from economists, and 3 experts with experience. (5) Regarding the local system: 1. In order to realize the advocacy of shared governance through balanced power, the provinces of the country shall be divided into several political zones, each with a political committee. 2. The municipal areas and powers of the provinces should be reduced. 3. To actively promote county-level local self-government. (6) Supplementary provisions: 1. The candidate for Chairman should be someone of high age, virtue, and prestige. 2. The President of the Executive Yuan should be someone who is intelligent, capable, and able to rectify government affairs. 3. The Minister of Foreign Affairs should be someone with a revolutionary history who can implement revolutionary diplomacy. 4. The Minister of Finance should be someone with rich financial management experience and knowledge, not limited to party members. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central News Agency said that the report that Li Shizeng was ill and did not attend, and firmly declined to be a representative, is purely unfounded. Mr. Li was unable to attend yesterday due to illness, and there was no such thing as firmly declining to be a representative. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Nanjing side believes that the Central Government's political system plan for the Guangdong representatives violates the party constitution and cannot be discussed, and the prospects for peace are pessimistic. (30th Special Dispatch)

The Central Government Announces the Peace Process with Guangdong

(Nanjing) The arrival of the Guangdong representatives in Shanghai to discuss peace and unity has attracted much attention from the people. Regarding this matter, in late September, the Central Government, considering the urgency of the national crisis and the need for unity against foreign aggression, Chiang Kai-shek personally sent a letter to Wang Jingwei, Gu Mengyu, and Sun Ke, entrusting Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Puquan, and Chen Zhenru to bring it to Guangzhou, asking them to work together to save the country from danger, and orally conveyed three principles. After Cai and others arrived in Hong Kong, they sent a telegram on the 29th, reporting on two agreed-upon measures: (1) Chiang Kai-shek issues a circular telegram stating his resignation due to the agreement on unified government measures, and the Guangdong side also issues a circular telegram expressing its willingness to go to Beijing for a meeting, cancel the Guangzhou government, and not make Chiang Kai-shek's resignation a condition; (2) Change the garrison organization of Nanjing and Shanghai. They then sent another telegram hoping that Chen Mingshu would be responsible for the garrison of Nanjing and Shanghai. After receiving the telegram, the Central Government immediately made the appointment and sent a telegram to report it. On October 1st, Cai and others sent another telegram stating that the circular telegrams must be published on the 5th. Chiang Kai-shek replied on the 2nd, reiterating the three principles and hoping to invite them to come quickly. Afterwards, there were several exchanges and consultations. The Guangdong representatives arrived in Shanghai on the 21st of this month. However, the Central Government is eager for them to come to Beijing as soon as possible to jointly overcome the national crisis. The letters and telegrams sent by Cai and others to Hong Kong a month ago are excerpted below to show the initial consultation process.

(1) Chiang Kai-shek's letter to Wang Jingwei, Gu Mengyu, Sun Ke, etc., forwarded to all comrades by Jingwei, Xiangqin, Zhesheng, and others: Unfortunately, the party and the country are facing successive natural and man-made disasters. Recently, the Northeast has been invaded and plundered, the army has been defeated, and the country is in imminent danger. Our party, inheriting the teachings of Sun Yat-sen and entrusted by the people, has led the country into deep water and fire, and the fate of the nation is about to be lost. The guilt is severe, and how can we face Sun Yat-sen and the people? Looking around the party, we are aroused by emotional disputes and mistakes, each going to extremes, resulting in today's tragic disaster of national hatred. The grief is extreme. Today, fellow countrymen are weeping and telling each other that there is no way to save the country from danger without the whole country working together. Moreover, we share the revolutionary mission, so what cannot be sacrificed? Let us all overcome the national crisis. As a country for three years, the sins have accumulated. The rights and wrongs of the past, I am willing to bear them alone. What more can I ask for? I only hope that all comrades will put the party first, think of the imminent danger, reflect on themselves, meet each other with sincerity, and not let past grudges become obstacles. Let us save this tragic disaster of a leaking boat and a collapsing nest, lest the thousands of years of the divine race be cut off from us, and the tragedy of national subjugation be attributed to Sun Yat-sen's disregard for internal strife and the neglect of the national crisis. Then I will regard humiliation as a special honor. I specially entrust comrades Cai, Zhang, and Chen to go to Hong Kong to discuss everything. This paper cannot exhaust my sincere blood in the slightest. Zhenru must convey the requests of all comrades here in a roundabout way, and fully represent them. (This letter was handed over to the three representatives Cai, Zhang, and Chen to carry.)

(2) Telegram from Zhang, Cai, and Chen after arriving in Hong Kong: To Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Nanjing, Shu and others arrived in Hong Kong yesterday. Comrade Fu Bingchang came to the ship to greet us and informed us that comrades Wang Jingwei, Sun Zhesheng, and Li Wenfan would arrive in Hong Kong at 5:00 PM. The three comrades arrived as scheduled. We started discussing at 6:00 PM, handed over your handwritten letter, and the three comrades felt your sincerity and exchanged opinions sincerely until 11:00 PM. Although the outline is already available, there are still a few points that are not very well agreed upon. It was agreed to continue the discussion at 9:00 AM this morning. We reconvened at the appointed time and reached an agreement at 11:30 AM: (1) You will issue a circular telegram, citing the urgency of the situation, taking the blame, and stating that you will immediately step down when the unified government measures are agreed upon. The Guangdong side will also issue a circular telegram, also apologizing to the people and saying that only unification can save the country, going to Beijing for a meeting, and canceling the Guangzhou government, and not making your resignation a condition. The two telegrams must be published simultaneously. The drafts of the telegrams are being drafted and will be telegraphed immediately. At present, both parties have instructed party departments and newspapers at all levels to stop mutual attacks. (2) The garrison and guard organization of Nanjing and Shanghai must be changed immediately so that comrades from Guangdong can come to Beijing with peace of mind, take an oath at Sun Yat-sen's mausoleum to hold a meeting, and decide on unified government measures. Is this appropriate? Waiting for instructions. Pei Jishu bows respectfully at noon.

(3) Chiang's telegram to Cai, Zhang, and Chen: To General Commander Chen of Guangzhou, Brother Zhenru, and forwarded to the two gentlemen Cai and Zhang, China has only one government. Only by unifying China can we save the country from foreign aggression. At this time of national survival, we must seek a satisfactory solution in terms of reason and morality. Therefore, I have specially agreed with you on the following three principles: (1) If Guangdong can take full responsibility, then the central comrades can give way completely. Please ask the comrades in Guangdong to move to the capital as a whole and reorganize the government. As for my personal resignation, there is no problem. As long as Guangdong can reliably take over, I can send a telegram to resign. This is the first one. (2) If Guangdong cannot take responsibility, then the Central Government should be responsible for presiding over it, and the Guangdong government should be canceled. The Guangdong comrades should gather in the capital to jointly overcome the national crisis. This is the second one. (3) If all parties want to cooperate, then I would be even more welcome, but they must come to Beijing to discuss it in person. This is the way to be sincere and help each other in the same boat. Apart from these three, if we must make conditional demands, then it is unreasonable, immoral, and contrary to public and private interests. This is not what I want to hear. You have forgotten these three principles and the three words "unconditionally," and you have sent this telegram with no room for negotiation. I don't know what it means, which is really puzzling. Moreover, after the Central Government received your telegram, considering it was beneficial to the party and the country and the basis for cooperation, it immediately appointed Brother Zhen as the garrison commander. This is why we are unwilling to have conditions and eager to cooperate sincerely. Now, if the comrades in Guangdong do not seek a solution in reason, morality, and national crisis, and cannot come here to discuss it in person, then sending a telegram first will only cause more disputes and will not help. I hope you will sincerely discuss this with the comrades based on the above intentions so that it can be resolved completely. Chiang Kai-shek, winter army. (30th Central News Agency Telegram)

If the party remains fragmented and the country remains divided, the party will inevitably cease to be a party, and the country will cease to be a country. I am deeply concerned about this. I sincerely hope that you will both embrace the doctrine of sacrifice, strive to complete the party as a whole, the unified country, and work together to resist foreign aggression to save the country from danger." (Nanjing) The National Government Flood Relief Association established an office in the Ning District in Nanjing, hiring Ling Daoyang as a relief commissioner to handle relief affairs in the six counties of Ning District. Its organization is divided into six sections: Treasury, Audit, Warehouse, Transportation Engineering, Employee Agricultural Relief. Now that American wheat is being transported to Nanjing, the "work for food" plan will be implemented. The amount of American wheat distributed to Nanjing is about 150,000 tons. A general distribution center for American wheat will be set up in Nanjing, and all relief wheat in Jiangning, Zhenjiang, Wuhu, and other districts will be distributed by the center. The first batch of American wheat to be received in Ning District is about 500 tons and is expected to arrive in the middle of next month. Foreigners Entering the Country Must Have Passports Verified

(Nanjing) Staff from the International Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs discussed the verification of passports for foreigners entering the country. Due to the initial leniency, it was handled with flexibility. Regulations stipulated that those without visas within three months would be temporarily allowed to apply for visas with a fee. Foreigners already residing in the country would be allowed to have their passports stamped for free as proof of residence. This measure has been repeatedly extended until the end of October this year. Starting November 1st, all entry passports without visas must be processed according to Rule 4. For those residing locally without visas, a fee will be charged for visa applications starting from the 1st. Subsequently, when foreigners travel inland and apply for passports or request visa extensions on their original passports, they must simultaneously present their entry passports. (30th Dispatch)

Puyi's Divorce Case Resolved

(Tianjin) Jin Yanxiu, the Shufei (Consort) of the abdicated Emperor Puyi, fled in the autumn and requested a divorce. Foreign News

British Cabinet Prepares for Reorganization

Cabinet Members to Increase to Twenty

A Shift Possible in the Foreign Affairs Portfolio

Industrial Activity Showing Signs of Life

Tariff Policy Determined to Proceed

Reuters, London, 29th - After returning from Buckingham Palace, Prime Minister MacDonald immediately consulted with Lord Sankey, the Lord Chancellor, and Sir William Jowitt, the Attorney General, on procedural matters. Today, he will meet with cabinet members Snowden, Thomas, Baldwin, and Samuel. It is reported that MacDonald is determined to make the new cabinet a completely national one, as the election was a mandate for the National Government, not for any particular party. Therefore, he believes that labor should have adequate representation in the cabinet.

Reuters, London, 29th - This afternoon, cabinet members reconvened on Downing Street, the first gathering after the election. All attendees were in high spirits and smiling, unlike the initial gatherings of the National Government, which were filled with concern. Samuel of the Liberal Party met with MacDonald for half an hour before the gathering.

It is widely expected that the government's first task will be the reorganization of the cabinet. The pre-election National Cabinet, limited to ten members, was considered insufficient in number. It will now be increased to twenty. Snowden, the Chancellor of the Exchequer, who had previously stated that he should not be selected, will likely be ennobled as a member of the House of Lords so that he can continue to serve as a cabinet member and assist the government, but he will no longer serve as Chancellor of the Exchequer. Who will succeed him as Chancellor is yet to be determined. Neville Chamberlain and Sir John Reith are the two most talked about candidates. The former is an important figure in the Conservative Party, and the latter is a shipping magnate, but Neville Chamberlain is considered more likely. There are many rumors circulating, but nothing has been finalized. However, Sir John Simon of the Liberal Party will likely occupy a position in the new cabinet. Newspapers speculate about the cabinet reshuffle, predicting that Baldwin will remain Lord President of the Council, Lister will be President of the Board of Trade, and Snowden, after being ennobled, will be Lord Privy Seal. A shift may also occur in the Foreign Affairs portfolio, currently held by Lord Reading. Lord Hailsham will likely regain his old position, replacing Sankey as Lord Chancellor. As for Secretary of State for War Crew and First Lord of the Admiralty Austen Chamberlain, they may retire to make way for younger people. Prime Minister MacDonald's first public remarks since the reopening of Parliament are likely to be delivered at the Lord Mayor's Banquet in London on November 11th. It is anticipated that his words will be highly significant. After the National Government's victory, there is hope for industrial recovery. There are signs of activity in various places. Many British manufacturers are now planning to reorganize their factories to accept new orders, while foreign manufacturers, anticipating a tariff policy, are urgently preparing to establish factories in Britain. Many agents are currently seeking suitable sites. At the same time, it is expected that before restrictions are placed on imported goods, a large number of foreign goods will be dumped into the country. The government must organize a special committee to study economic matters so that it can submit legislation on imported goods as early as possible after the new Parliament opens. However, the real work is likely to be implemented only in late January. Therefore, the government may propose urgent legislation to give it the power to stop dumping.

Tensions Between Poland and Lithuania

National News Agency, Warsaw, 29th - Large-scale anti-Lithuanian demonstrations were held simultaneously today in Warsaw, the capital of Poland, and Vilna. The reason is that Lithuania is oppressing the Polish minority within Lithuania. Since these unfortunate events occurred, the Polish and Lithuanian government authorities have repeatedly argued with each other. Now that anti-Lithuanian demonstrations have occurred throughout Poland, Lithuania has requested that they be suppressed, but this request has now been sternly rejected by the Polish government. Therefore, tensions between Poland and Lithuania have greatly increased again.

United States Accepts One-Year Arms Stoppage Proposal

Reuters, Washington, 29th - The United States has accepted the League of Nations proposal for a one-year suspension of arms construction. Today, the US government telegraphed its approval of this plan to Geneva.

Establishment of German Economic Advisory Council

Parliament Approves Minting of New Silver Coins

National News Agency, Berlin, 29th - Today, the advisory council of the German President's Office held its first meeting. President Hindenburg delivered a very sincere speech, urging the nation to unite. Hindenburg said that the hope for Germany's future is closely related to changes in the international community. The global political and economic situation is the foundation of Germany's political and economic situation. Therefore, Germany's diplomatic policy focuses on this point. However, diplomatic policy alone cannot place the nation on a solid foundation. The responsibility of the people is not reduced as a result. Therefore, regardless of the international situation or the state of the country, domestic unity is paramount. Everyone must exert their efforts, overcome differences, and cooperate internationally, starting domestically. Only in this way can we hope for the restoration of the motherland. After Hindenburg's speech, Prime Minister Brüning outlined the winter defense plan. Finance Minister Warmbold and the President of the German National Bank, Luther, also expressed their sincere views on the current situation. The Presidential Advisory Council was recently established and will subsequently meet once a day in a closed-door format.

Reuters, Berlin, 30th - The German Parliament has approved the minting of new silver coins up to a value of 120 million marks in order to assist the National Bank in managing the gold standard and reducing the amount of paper currency. This measure is in accordance with a policy that has been in progress for some time. Since the implementation of this policy, the import of silver bars has increased greatly.

Pilsudski Suddenly Returns Home

National News Agency, Warsaw, 30th - General Pilsudski of Poland suddenly returned home today after visiting Romania for two weeks to continue the Polish-Romanian military alliance. He had originally planned to stay in the Romanian capital for at least three weeks and then travel to Egypt. The sudden return caused widespread surprise and suspicion. Some said that the government, in light of the widespread strikes, feared that they would cause domestic political unrest and asked Pilsudski to return to restore order. Others said that Pilsudski had to return to the capital due to the results of the British general election.

Persia Signs Treaty on the Manufacture of Narcotics

Reuters, Geneva, 30th - According to official sources today, Persia has signed the 1931 treaty on the manufacture of narcotics.

Estimate of Edison's Estate

Approximately US$12 million

Reuters, New York, 29th - Edison's will leaves most of his estate to his two sons by his second wife. It is expected that they will divide it with the children of Edison's first wife. The will did not mention his wife, as she had already received a large sum during his lifetime. The total value of Edison's estate has not yet been announced, but newspapers estimate it to be approximately US$12 million.

After Zhang Haipeng's Failure

The Japanese Use Mongolian Bandits and Korean Ruffians to Cause Trouble

Harbin Correspondence: The purpose of the Japanese military advance this time is to create a new separatist government in the three northeastern provinces to serve as a tool of their imperialism. Before the League of Nations issued its recommendations, they had already created the Jilin Chief Executive Office of Xi Qia and the maintenance associations of 鬫朝璽 (Kan Chao-hsi) and others. Although these two organizations do not have much power, they can still use a donkey to scare the Northeastern people with a tiger skin. However, Heilongjiang Province has Wan Guobin, the son of Wan Fulin, sitting in charge, and it has remained unmoved. The Special District of Eastern Province also has relations with Soviet Russia, so they have been unable to do as they wish. Therefore, they took the opportunity to control the Siping-Taonan and Taonan-Ang'angxi railways to create a new evil force. Zhang Haipeng, the garrison commander of Taonan, was deceived by them.

Zhang Haipeng was originally on the same level as Zhang Zuolin, Zhang Zuoxiang, and Zhang Jinghui. After the founding of the Republic of China, Zhang Zuolin became the Grand Marshal, and Zhang Zuoxiang and Zhang Jinghui had reached the highest ranks, but he was still only a garrison commander in a remote area. He was truly unwilling to accept this. In the past, he reorganized the Peng and Xu regiments under Huang Xiansheng to strengthen his forces, indicating his unwillingness to remain a lowly official. However, at that time, Zhang Zuolin's power was like an iron bucket. Later, Zou Zuohua's troops were stationed in Xing'an for land reclamation, and their power was above his, which made Zhang Haipeng even more unhappy. This time, when the Japanese sent troops, Zhang believed it was a heaven-sent opportunity, and the Japanese were constantly sending him signals of affection. Therefore, he had to become a disloyal traitor.

Initially, the Japanese also thought they had a great chance of success, as they still remembered the good dream of the Eastern Three Provinces red beards helping them during the Russo-Japanese War. During the Russo-Japanese War, the Japanese had received assistance from bandits. Therefore, this time, before sending troops, the Japanese spent more than 200,000 Japanese yen to incite bandits. However, there are many heroes among the bandits, such as the proclamations issued by gang leaders such as Gai Sansheng to sacrifice themselves for the country, which is proof of this. This time, the Japanese used Zhang Haipeng because they thought that Zhang was originally a figure from the old Green Forest and would be easy to use. Zhang, in addition to being misled by the Japanese, was also deceived by the remnants of the fallen Qing Dynasty, such as Prince Gong Puwei. After Puwei and others were active in Shenyang, they preemptively appointed Zhang as the general of Heilongjiang. Therefore, Zhang's index finger moved greatly. Two trainloads of Japanese military supplies were transported to Taonan in the late night of the 10th and 11th of this month and handed over to Zhang.

After Zhang Haipeng obtained military supplies and the assistance of Mongolian bandits (skilled riders), he instructed Peng and Xu, the commanders of his two regiments, to prepare. The two regimental commanders were still hesitant. On the 12th of this month, 300 Japanese soldiers arrived from Nankai and exerted great pressure on Zhang, ordering him to mobilize. Zhang had no choice but to order Peng and Xu to mobilize. The two regimental commanders replied that they dared not disobey the orders of the garrison commander, but they feared that if they saw the garrison commander again after this trip, they would not be able to speak. The two regimental commanders left, but the troops were still slow to advance (later turning their weapons against Zhang). The Japanese soldiers were worried that the delay would cause problems, so they forced Zhang and his confidants to board the train and head north. However, the Black Army had already prepared for the opportunity. The Yu Zhaolin brigade stationed on the banks of the Nen River retreated to the left bank of the river, destroyed the bridge, and defended it. Upon seeing the enemy, they immediately fired artillery to resist. Zhang's troops had never received training and saw that they were fighting for the Japanese invaders, so they had no fighting spirit. At the sound of gunfire, they scattered. The Japanese soldiers' encouragement was ineffective, and they were also afraid that the reclamation army (Zou Zuohua's troops) would cut off their rear, so they escorted the remaining soldiers straight back to Zhendong (more than 100 li away from Taonan). 　　, a Japanese advisor to the East Special Chief Executive Office in Harbin, made this trip in vain.

On the evening of the 20th, Ma Zhanshan, the newly appointed acting chairman of Heilongjiang Province and the former garrison commander of Heihe, disguised himself and took a boat from Heihe. He changed trains at Duiqingshan on the way to Longsha and took office on the morning of the 21st. About a brigade of his troops had also arrived in Heihe. The Black Army's Su Bingwen's Hailun-Manchuria Railway Protection Brigade had also arrived. With the addition of these two fresh forces, Zhang Haipeng fell and could not rise again. The Japanese, seeing Zhang's failure, were deeply afraid that their process of division would be difficult to implement from then on. Therefore, on the one hand, they tried their best to help the Mongolian bandits to disturb the local area, destroy the Datong Road, and sever the connection between Jinzhou and Heilongjiang Province, using it as an excuse to control. On the other hand, they also spread rumors that the Taonan was suffering from a *pestis minor* epidemic to prevent foreigners from going to investigate the truth. On the other hand, they recruited tens of thousands of ruffians in Korea and escorted them to Dalian by warship on the night of the 12th and 13th. At that time, the entire city of Dalian was blacked out for tens of minutes to prevent the people from noticing. Currently, these Korean ruffians are all armed. Some of them are scattered along the Beining Railway to cause trouble and provide an excuse for the future. A part of them are used to replenish Zhang Haipeng's troops and were transported to Taonan in batches on the 15th and 16th. After Zhang's troops are replenished, conflicts are still likely to occur on the Taonan-Ang'angxi Railway. (22nd)

The Japanese "Pending Issues" Are Like This

They Claim We Violated Treaties

All Based on the Japanese Side's One-Sided Reasoning

A dispatch from Beiping states that after occupying Liaoning and Jilin, the Japanese army publicly proclaimed that there were over three hundred pending issues between China and Japan, and that China had disregarded treaties and intentionally delayed resolution, inciting the anger of the entire Japanese population and leading to the occupation of Liaoning and Jilin. They claimed that to resolve all pending issues, they had to guarantee their occupation, awaken the Chinese side, and hope for an early resolution. At the time, we suspected that the Japanese government's statement was an exaggeration, and that there were not three hundred pending issues. Furthermore, we had never violated any treaties. We searched and investigated extensively, hoping to obtain the exact number and report it to our readers, to demonstrate the Japanese talent for exaggeration and as a reference for future negotiations. However, after a month of effort, it was difficult to find. Although we knew some of the issues, we felt we did not have the whole picture. The delay continued until today, failing to satisfy our readers' expectations. Now, we have learned from reliable Japanese sources that the so-called instances of China infringing upon Japan's rights and interests in Manchuria and Mongolia, including the Nakamura Incident, amount to only fifty-four cases. Among them, some are minor, some are unreasonable, some are based on the Twenty-One Demands, which our entire nation has rejected, or they are based on the expired Sino-Japanese Treaty Concerning Manchuria. For example, regarding the stationing of troops along the South Manchurian Railway, Japan inherited this right from the Sino-Russian Treaty. The Sino-Japanese Agreement on Manchuria clearly stipulated that if Russia withdrew its troops from the Chinese Eastern Railway, Japan should follow suit. After the old Sino-Russian Treaty was abolished, Japan not only failed to fulfill its treaty obligations but also used the treaty to accuse us of violating it. Such examples are numerous. We now present the complete list of the fifty-four instances of China infringing upon Japan's interests, as claimed by the Japanese. Readers should understand the intentions of the Japanese and quickly study and refute them.

1. Construction of the parallel lines of the Datong and Xifeng (Xi'an to Dongfeng) Railways: (A) China began construction on the Datong line in August of the fifteenth year of Taisho (August of the fourteenth year of the Republic of China), disregarding the South Manchurian Railway's repeated protests, and continued the construction, starting provisional operations on November 15th of the second year of Showa (sixteenth year of the Republic of China). (B) In January of the first year of Showa (fifteenth year of the Republic of China), construction began on the Jihai branch line, approximately 40 miles from Beishanchengzi to Dongfeng, disregarding the protest of the Fengtian Consul-General and completing the construction by the end of the same year.

2. Disregard of the agreement regarding the extension of the Beining Railway. Regarding the violation of Article 6 of the agreement on the extension of the Beining Railway, the connecting trains between the Beining Line and the South Manchurian Railway first stopped at Shenyang Station and then proceeded to the South Manchurian Railway's Fengtian Station.

3. The construction of the Jihai Line is a one-sided trampling of the provisions of the preliminary contract for loans for the four railways of Manchuria and Mongolia. China arbitrarily constructed the Jihai Line, which was completed in May of the fourth year of Showa (eighteenth year of the Republic of China).

4. The Changda Line and trampling of the construction contracts for the Jihui Line, etc. Regarding the Changda Line (Changchun to Daliao) and Dunhui Line (Dunhua to Haining), which were concluded in May of the third year of Showa (seventeenth year of the Republic of China) with the Ministry of Communications, the South Manchurian Railway intended to begin work in reality, but China blocked it at an inopportune time, preventing the start of construction.

5. Illegal restriction of the authority of the T'ao-Ang Railway advisor. In violation of the attached exchange of letters to the T'ao-Ang Railway loan contract, China did not grant the advisor dispatched by the South Manchurian Railway to the T'ao-Ang Railway the authority stipulated.

6. Failure to hire a chief accountant for the Jidun Railway. China violated the Jidun Construction Contract, failing to hire a Japanese chief accountant for the Jidun Railway, and appointing a Chinese accountant to this day.

7. Regarding the connection equipment between Tongliao and Datong on the Siping-Taonan Railway: The Datong Line was constructed regardless of Japanese protests and became a parallel line to the South Manchurian Railway. Japan has a major interest in the extension line from Tongliao, and the connection equipment construction between the Siping-Taonan and Datong lines is closely related to the extension line. According to the meeting held in Tianjin in December of the fifth year of Showa between Japan and China regarding the Beining (Datong) and Siping-Taonan Railways, it was decided to implement the connection equipment. Because of repeated reminders from the Chinese side after the railway began negotiations, it was clear that the issue of the connection equipment and other issues should be properly addressed. The request for connection equipment was to be put on hold, but China disregarded this and completed the connection equipment without notification.

8. Denial of the South Manchurian Railway-Siping-Taonan Railway connection agreement. The connection transportation contract between the South Manchurian Railway and the Siping-Taonan Railway Bureau was signed in September of the third year of Showa. The revision of the South Manchurian Railway's contract for connecting cargo transport via the Korean Railway and the Siping-Taonan Railway is inseparably related to this contract. The approval of the Communications Committee has not been obtained to this day, and the two contracts remain shelved, and Japan has not yet revised them.

9. The hardships of the Jidun Line and Tao'an Line construction: Regarding the construction costs of 34 million yuan for the Jidun Line (completed in October of the third year of Showa) and 12.92 million yuan for the Tao'an Line (completed in June of the second year of Showa), China pleaded hardship and has not yet been able to determine the amounts.

10. Obstructing the South Manchurian Railway, approximately 90 incidents per year: As a result of the Chinese authorities' inadequate enforcement, the South Manchurian Railway suffered the following obstructions in Manchuria and outside the prefecture in the fourth and fifth years of Showa (the number of incidents decreased in the fifth year due to special efforts by the Japanese to prevent them):

Year Obstructions Number of Transport Obstructions Thefts of Railway Supplies Theft of Electric Wires

Damage Incidents Property Stolen Number of Items Times

Showa 4 87 114 17 13

Showa 5 84 75 5 15

11. Improper taxation of South Manchurian Railway materials: In violation of Article 8 of the attached agreement to the South Manchurian Railway Treaty, since February of the second year of Showa, half of the wood tax has been levied on the Chinese sellers of Jilin-produced sleepers used by the South Manchurian Railway.

12. Illegal restrictions on the purchase of South Manchurian Railway materials: In the third year of Showa, the South Manchurian Railway Company purchased hundreds of thousands of sleepers. China considered this amount excessive and did not issue the necessary number of tax-exempt passports. It took a year of protest and negotiation to issue them all.

13. Obstructing the South Manchurian Railway's use of stone materials: According to Article 6 of the "Contract for the Construction and Management of the Chinese Eastern Railway," regarding the quarrying sites for railway stones, the Japanese right to lease land has been comprehensively agreed upon. Recently, the Chinese side has obstructed it by all means. (To be continued)

Shenyang Financial and Industrial Bureaus Established Under Japanese Influence

Both Bureaus Form Reorganization Committees

Real Power Entirely in Japanese Hands

A dispatch from Harbin states that the previous dispatch detailed the restoration of the Shenyang Financial and Industrial Bureaus. Here are the regulations of the two bureaus:

(A) Industrial Bureau, Chapter 1: General Principles (1) The Local Maintenance Committee, to guide and control the various industries necessary for maintaining the people's livelihood, will establish temporary measures as an emergency plan until the new regime is firmly established, to allow the Industrial Bureau to open. Chapter 2: Organization and Authority (1) The Local Maintenance Committee will quickly decide on the Director of the Industrial Bureau. (2) The organization and authority of the Industrial Bureau will temporarily follow the previous system, but limited to the minimum necessary. (3) To ensure the thoroughness of the industrial administrative plan, the Local Maintenance Committee may hire several Japanese advisors and consultants to enrich the advisors and consultants of the Industrial Bureau. Chapter 3: Control of Industry (1) The Local Maintenance Committee will establish an Industrial Planning Committee to formulate implementation plans for various industrial guidance and controls. The organization is as follows: Japanese representatives, representatives of the Local Maintenance Committee, the Director of the Financial Bureau, the Financial Bureau's advisors, the Director of the Industrial Bureau, the heads of each department, advisors, representatives of the Municipal Public Office, representatives of the Provincial Farmers' Association, and representatives of the Provincial Chamber of Commerce. Supplementary Provisions (1) The Director of the Industrial Bureau, in order to achieve its objectives, may consult the Local Maintenance Committee and promptly issue necessary announcements. However, in its implementation, it must first receive the approval of the Japanese army. (2) The Local Maintenance Committee will stipulate temporary measures for the Industrial Bureau, and based on this, petition the Japanese army in advance to open the Industrial Bureau. Once approved, it will immediately begin. (3) Regarding financial assistance to those who are hostile, the Local Maintenance Committee may severely punish them based on its decision.

(B) Financial Bureau, Chapter 1: General Principles, Article 1: The Local Maintenance Committee recognizes that the revival of the Financial Bureau is necessary to ensure public order and restore people's livelihoods before the establishment of the new regime, and will formulate temporary measures based on its responsibilities to achieve this goal. Chapter 2: Organization and Authority, Article 2: The Local Maintenance Committee will decide on the candidate for Director of the Financial Bureau. Article 3: The organization and authority of the Financial Bureau will temporarily follow the previous system, but must be limited to the minimum necessary. Article 4: To manage finances and improve them, the Local Maintenance Committee will recruit several Japanese advisors and consultants. The Director of the Financial Bureau must respect the opinions of the advisors and consultants regarding the operation of financial administration. Chapter 3: Financial Reorganization, Article 5: The Local Maintenance Committee will establish a Financial Reorganization Committee to formulate and revise tax regulations, compile budgets, and make other plans. The scope of the committee members is as follows: Japanese representatives, representatives of the Local Maintenance Committee, the Director of the Financial Bureau, advisors, department heads, consultants, representatives of the Municipal Public Office, representatives of the Provincial Chamber of Commerce, and representatives of the Provincial Farmers' Association (limited to when revising the tax system). Supplementary Provisions, Article 6: The Director of the Financial Bureau must consult the Local Maintenance Committee and promptly issue necessary announcements on his own. When implementing them, he must first receive the approval of the Japanese army. Article 7: The Local Maintenance Committee will stipulate temporary measures for the Financial Bureau and request the Japanese army in advance for approval to open the bureau, and then begin quickly. Article 8: If tax officials from the old regime deliver various tax payments, the Maintenance Committee, through its resolution, will request the Japanese military authorities to severely punish them. Observing these two regulations, it is known that the Japanese army is intensifying its management in Shenyang step by step and embarking on a permanent plan. Although the League of Nations has limited its troop withdrawal to three weeks, it is feared that it is just an empty statement, and the Japanese side is still ignoring it. What will become of China? (24th)

Guangzhou Registers Shops Selling Japanese Goods

Thoroughly Cutting Off Imports of Japanese Goods

A dispatch from Guangzhou states that since the Japanese invasion of the East, the people of Guangdong have been extremely indignant. Various counties and cities have launched anti-Japanese movements, implementing economic severance with Japan. The academic community has also organized anti-Japanese volunteer armies. The people's spirit is flourishing like wildfire. Since the establishment of the All Circles Anti-Japanese Association in Guangzhou, the anti-Japanese salvation associations previously organized by various groups have successively ended and unanimously joined the All Circles Anti-Japanese Association to achieve unity. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce recently, in order to cut off imports of Japanese goods,

Page 9

specially drafted measures for registering shops selling enemy goods and submitted them to the All Circles Anti-Japanese Conference for resolution and implementation. After the conference passed them, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce printed and distributed the registration forms for enemy goods, requiring all shops to register their existing Japanese goods from November 1st to the 5th. Those who register falsely or incompletely, or who fail to report within the deadline, will be investigated for smuggling Japanese goods. Here are the registration measures for enemy goods of the association: (1) The period from November 1st to November 5th is the period for all shops in Guangzhou to register their existing Japanese goods. (2) All shops in Guangzhou, if they have Japanese goods in stock that have not been sold, regardless of the amount, must register them on schedule. (3) The registration items must be filled in and reported according to the registration form set by the association. (4) The registration forms are prepared by the association and distributed to various trade associations, and kept at the association for shops to use. (5) The various shops belonging to the various trade associations fill out four copies of the registration form, keep one copy for themselves, and submit the remaining three copies to the trade association of that industry. The trade association will extract two copies and submit them to the association for separate storage and transfer to the Guangdong All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Congress. (6) Shops that have not formed trade associations must fill out three copies of the registration form, keep one copy for themselves, and submit the remaining two copies directly to the association for separate storage and transfer to the Guangdong All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Congress. (7) If any shop registers falsely or fails to register within the deadline, once discovered and verified, the association will consult with the Guangdong All Circles National Salvation Congress to investigate them for smuggling enemy goods. (8) After the registration period expires, the association will, together with the Guangdong All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Congress, send personnel to the shops to check the goods. If there is no concealment, the association will post a "Registration Completed" sign on the shop's door for identification. If the shop is a wholesale business, and the goods are sold in whole boxes or packages, the Guangdong All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Congress will issue a registration stamp for the goods to be affixed to the surface of the goods when they are sold for inspection. (9) After the registration is completed, all shops that sell Japanese goods must report their sales every five days. The sales report form will be prepared and distributed by the association for use. The number of copies to be filled out each time and the submission procedures are the same as for the registration form. (10) When the Japanese goods registered by each shop are sold out, the association will prepare a sign saying "Japanese Goods Sold Out, No More Enemy Goods Sold Hereafter" and affix it to the shop's door to show their determination to save the country. (11) The association will not collect funds or any fees for handling the registration of existing Japanese goods in the shops. (October 25th)

Propagating to Various Countries in French, English, and German

Hosting Belgian Celebrities and the Press

A dispatch from Brussels states that upon hearing the bad news of Japan's military deployment in the Northeast, the overseas Chinese in Belgium were all indignant. Zhang Zuoren, representing Brussels, Lu Bingxiong, representing Leuven, Shen Chenglin, representing Ghent, An Zhongyi, representing Liege, and Zhang Anya, representing Charleroi, were elected as executive committee members, responsible for handling all motions of the delegate conference. On October 6th, the Executive Committee also held a reception at the Central Hotel in Brussels, inviting Belgian celebrities and journalists. Professor Maoqi then stood up and gave a speech, saying that he had stayed in China for more than ten years, read many Chinese books, such as Laozi, Zhuangzi, Confucius, and Mencius, and that Chinese philosophy is based purely on peace and justice, with customs that are honest and kind, and people who are benevolent and patient. China is indeed the center of Eastern civilization and the source of world culture. This time, the incident in the Northeast proves that Japan harbors aggressive ambitions, which is extremely obvious. We express our deep sympathy to China and are willing to fight against the tyrannical to realize world peace and happiness. President Otter then gave a speech, saying that the incident in the Northeast gave us a profound impression. The world should intervene in Japan's violent behavior. We first hope that the League of Nations can suppress this behavior that harms humanity based on justice. Secondly, we further imagine using this opportunity to unite all the people of the world and organize an international institution to solve the events that the League of Nations cannot solve. If everything is made public, peace will be realized. Finally, the chairman shouted "Long live Belgium, long live the Republic of China, long live the people of the world!" and the event ended happily.

The matters discussed were: (1) The standing committee proposed, "The drafting of the regulations to punish traitorous merchants, drafted by Committee Member Xia, has been reviewed and revised once by the standing committee. Is it appropriate? Please vote on the proposal." The resolution was passed. (2) The standing committee proposed, "The third standing committee's resolution suggested that the executive committee raise donations based on Article 19 of the Outline and draft a donation appeal. Is it feasible? Please vote on the proposal." The resolution was passed to solicit donations from party, government, and military officials. The original text of the donation appeal was passed. Temporary Motions: (1) Committee Member Xia Yuxuan moved to ask when the investigation work should begin. It was resolved that: 1. The investigation should begin on November 1st. 2. Each middle and higher school should send five students to organize an investigation team. 3. During the investigation, three people should be sent from the trade association of that industry to accompany the investigation. 4. Committee Members Yan Shengmin, Xia Yuxuan, Li Dexuan, Wang Fuchen, Feng Zhensheng, Tang Caigan, and Chai Qisheng were elected to form an investigation committee of seven people. Committee Member Xia was responsible for convening the investigation section to convene. (2) Committee Member Wang Fuchen moved to ask whether Japanese goods ordered by various shops before August 20th could be shipped again. It was resolved that: The investigation section should publish in the newspaper that the registration forms must be submitted by the end of October, otherwise, the shop will be considered to have no Japanese goods. (3) Committee Member Zhang Jiyuan moved to propose that the association should send a telegram to Minister Shi Zhaoji urging him to fight for national rights and to persist to the end. The resolution was made that the general affairs section should draft a telegram and have it reviewed and sent by Committee Members Song, Xia, and He. (4) Committee Member Tang Caigan moved that the association should register members and issue symbols. The resolution was for the investigation section to handle it. (5) Committee Member Xia Yuxuan moved to propose that the propaganda section should set a date to start the propaganda campaign. It was resolved that it should start on November 1st. (6) Committee Member Song Dongfu moved to propose whether to proceed with the organization of a volunteer army. It was resolved that the organization section should draft other measures. (28th)

Shandong Provincial Government Takes Over National Tax Agencies

People Assigned by the Provincial Government to Handle Them

A dispatch from Jinan states that the various national tax agencies in Shandong Province, including the Salt Transport Commissioner's Office, the Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, the Consolidated Tax Administration Office, and the Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau, have all been taken over by the provincial government and will be managed by people assigned by the provincial government. Han Fuju, the chairman of the Shandong provincial government, appointed Li Wuchen (Chief of the Military Law Department of the Third Route Army Headquarters) as Acting Shandong Salt Transport Commissioner, Meng Zhaokong (Chief of the Military Supply Section of the Third Route Army Headquarters) as Acting Director of the Shandong Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, Hou Xitian (Chief Accounting Officer of the Provincial Government) as Acting Director of the Consolidated Tax Administration Office, and Tian Lianzhong (Deputy Chief of the Military Supply Section of the Third Route Army Headquarters) as Acting Director of the Shandong Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau this morning (28th). They are also responsible for taking over the tax payments and tax tickets stored in each office and bureau, preparing a detailed list of four columns, and submitting it for verification. After receiving the orders, the acting personnel went to take over their respective offices, and the situation is as follows:

Salt Transport Commissioner's Office: The former Salt Transport Commissioner Yuan Timing went to Beijing before the Mid-Autumn Festival and has not returned. His section chief was responsible for the handover. Yuan's personal belongings stored in the office have all been transported to Nanjing. The newly appointed Acting Salt Transport Commissioner Li Wuchen will officially take office tomorrow morning (29th).

Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau: The former Director of the Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau, Xiang Jieren, went to Beijing with Jiang Bocheng earlier and has not returned. His section chief was responsible for the handover. The newly appointed Acting Director Meng Zhaokong took over the seal and took office at 12:00 AM today (28th), and posted a notice of assumption of office saying, "According to the instructions of the Shandong Provincial Government, it is ordered to comply. The position of Director of the Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau has been entrusted to the said official to act. All payments for various types of stamps, tobacco, and alcohol stored in the bureau, as well as tax tickets, must be thoroughly investigated. For this reason, the Director of the Bureau is ordered to quickly list the items received separately in a detailed list of four columns and submit it for verification, and first report the date of arrival. Do not delay this order. In addition to submitting a separate report and holding an oath-taking ceremony to assume office, the merchants and residents are hereby notified."

Consolidated Tax Administration Office: The former Director of the Consolidated Tax Administration Office, Xu Tieshan, handed over the office today (28th). The new Director, Hou Xitian, visited the office in the morning and decided to officially go to the office tomorrow morning (29th).

Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau: The former Director, Ren Wenhan, handed over the office today (28th). The new Director, Tian Lianzhong, took over the office at noon and decided to officially work tomorrow (29th).

Regarding the reason why Shandong Province took over the national tax agencies, according to Han Fuju, the military pay of the headquarters has not been received for several months, and only a few hundred thousand were received in September, which is far from enough to maintain operations. Therefore, people were first sent to take over the various tax revenue agencies in order to maintain military pay. (28th)

Changshu

Joint Suppression of Bandits in Yangcheng Lake: A major robbery occurred in Mocheng Town, and 28 people were kidnapped. Except for 25 people who have been rescued from danger, the remaining three people are still in the hands of the bandits. The Department of Civilian Affairs considered this to be an unprecedented major case in Changshu and specially instructed Shen Weikuai, the third district chief of the Water Police Team, to rescue the remaining three hostages within three days. District Chief Shen recently learned that the gang of lake bandits had recently gathered again in Yangcheng Lake at the junction of Suzhou, Changshu, and Kunshan, and immediately telegraphed Yang Qingjiu, the thirteenth team leader of this county, to quickly lead his team from Kunshan. Then, he personally led the eleventh, fourteenth, and fifteenth teams from Suzhou to pursue the lake, converge with Yang's team, and take a surrounding posture to capture the bandits in one fell swoop. The thirteenth team set off on the morning of the 30th to suppress the bandits.

Kunshan

Provincial Order to Collect Land Tax for Road Construction: The Kunshan County Government has repeatedly received provincial orders to allocate the land tax collected for road construction to the purchase of government bonds for river management and transportation. Both the Finance and Construction Departments have sent representatives to Kunshan to oversee the collection. However, the county had already decided to use the road construction land tax to repair embankments as a form of work relief. If the province takes the funds, there will be no money for embankment repairs, which is extremely dangerous. After hearing the news, various agencies held meetings to discuss requesting the provincial committee to postpone the withdrawal. Representatives were sent to the province along with County Magistrate Pang to personally plead with Chairman Ye to allow the funds to be used for embankment repairs. The representatives have not yet returned to Kunshan, and the provincial government has sent an urgent telegram urging the withdrawal, stating that the payment of the government bonds for river management and transportation is important, and demanding that the land tax for road construction be quickly sent to the province.

Follow-up on Embezzlement of National Taxes Case: Hou Yiru, a tax collection officer in Kunshan, falsely listed a portion of the national taxes paid by various businesses over the years as owed by the people and embezzled the funds. This caused an uproar in society. A member of a certain party submitted a request to the party headquarters for a thorough investigation. The Executive Committee, considering the seriousness of the case, issued a public notice throughout the county, stating that if any business owner had paid national taxes and possessed receipts but could not find the corresponding grain receipts, they should submit the receipts to the committee for verification. The committee also requested the Finance Bureau to provide Hou's account books. On the 27th, an audit began. It was discovered that six households, including Tao Bohe, owed over 700 yuan in silver dollars from the Republic year 8. Tao and others were summoned to the meeting and stated that they had already paid in full and possessed receipts, but the receipts could not be matched. The committee members believed that the evidence of Hou's embezzlement of national taxes was conclusive. However, there were thousands of business owners in the county, and the embezzlement of over 700 yuan from six households in one year was alarming. It would take two or three months to settle these accounts. Yesterday, a letter was sent to the county government requesting that Hou be transferred to the judiciary for punishment and that the amount of embezzlement be clearly announced.

Chongming

Chongming and Qidong Counties Telegraph Request for Merger: The counties of Chongming and Qidong have recently faced massive administrative expenses, leading to a tenfold increase in national taxes. Furthermore, bandits and communists are everywhere, and the people are struggling to survive. Elders such as Ni Qinghe and Wang Qingmu from the two counties, seeking to reduce administrative expenses and lighten the burden on the people, had previously telegraphed the provincial government requesting a merger of the two counties, but without result. They now telegram again, stating that the separation of Chongming and Qidong was originally intended to unify county administration and reduce burdens. Now, a small number of people in Qidong have incited the people to surround the county magistrate and force him to send telegrams, seemingly willing to endure suffering rather than agree to a merger. The situation is incomprehensible, and it is hoped that this will be recognized. Local tyrants are behaving so rampantly that the people's happiness is being completely deprived. Wang Qingmu has been publicly nominated as a representative to present their views to the province. [Signed] Ni Qinghe and others.

Wuxi

Promptly Establish Temporary Courts to Try Crimes Endangering the Republic: The Jiangsu Higher Court had previously inquired with the Ministry of Justice, through the Pacification Commissioner's Office in Jiangsu Province, whether the Emergency Law for Punishing Crimes Endangering the Republic should be implemented in various counties according to bandit suppression areas. The reply stated that during the pacification period, bandit suppression and village cleansing were carried out simultaneously, and all pacification areas should be handled according to bandit suppression areas. An order was issued to various counties to comply. However, it has recently been found that many counties have delayed compliance, causing those accused of the above crimes to be detained without trial. This not only violates the purpose of the Emergency Law for Punishing Crimes but also greatly hinders the progress of cleaning up the officialdom. Yesterday, a special order was issued to various counties, reiterating the previous order that anyone who commits any of the crimes stipulated as endangering the Republic must be tried by a temporary court organized by the county magistrate and two judicial officials, according to Article 7 of the Emergency Law for Punishing Crimes. The temporary court is to be located in the county government, with the county magistrate as the presiding judge. The counties were ordered to present a request to the court within seven days of receiving the document to dispatch personnel to organize the temporary court and quickly conclude the trials without delay.

Implement General Inspection of Anti-Japanese Activities: The Wuxi Party Headquarters and various anti-Japanese national salvation associations had previously received requests from various industries, including silk, cloth, foreign goods, sundries, paper, hardware, etc., to allow a grace period for registering any remaining enemy goods in their stores that had not been fully registered. The committee decided to allow registration within five days, with a national salvation donation of 4% of the value of the goods. The deadline was the 28th. On the 29th, various industries submitted their registration forms through the Chamber of Commerce to the County Party Headquarters and the National Salvation Association for record-keeping. The Anti-Japanese Association's inspection department convened over 150 inspectors, assigned tasks, and launched a general mobilization on the afternoon of the 29th to conduct a general inspection simultaneously. In two days, a large quantity of cotton cloth, paper goods, and foreign goods were discovered. The goods will be dealt with according to the punishment rules after identification.

Attention to Fishery Administration: Jiangsu's fishery industry is largely run by chance, hindering its development. The Department of Agriculture, in order to promote development, is conducting a basic survey. Based on the principles of physical chemistry and biology, it is studying the movement and aggregation of fish to explore the location of fishing grounds and predict the prosperity or decline of the fishery. Fishermen's education is considered a key to rescuing fishermen and developing the fishery, so marine observation is being trialed, fishing experiments are being conducted continuously, and the Department of Education is collaborating to plan fishermen's education. Furthermore, the cotton woven netting used by fishermen is purchased from Japan, amounting to over a million yuan annually. In the midst of promoting domestic goods, all fishing boats are facing a standstill in going out to sea to fish due to a lack of netting. This has a major impact on the fishery. Special Envoy Hou Chaohai has been dispatched to liaise with Principal Jin of the Zhejiang Provincial Vocational School of Fisheries and General Manager Rong of the Sanxin Company to entrust the Shanghai Shenxin Textile Factory with manufacturing the netting. However, due to the small quantity and the large machinery, manufacturing is difficult, so the Shanghai Electric Weaving Factory has been contracted to produce the netting. After inspection and testing, it is found to be usable.

Xiaoshan

The Difficulty of Xiaoyi [Xiaoshan] Autonomy: Since the previous County Magistrate Du Shihua handled the land declaration, the local area has spent tens of thousands of yuan. Land disputes among the people have led to lawsuits and bankruptcy. The land declaration still has no effect. Since last year, an autonomous household tax has been created, assessed according to household, ranging from one yuan to ten yuan per year. Xiaoyi has suffered from repeated years of famine, and the people's strength is truly insufficient. This time, in order to establish a defense corps, ten yuan is assessed for every hundred households, forcibly apportioned to various townships, and the people are already complaining. Furthermore, 25% of every ten thousand yuan collected from the autonomy tax is used for district expenses, and 30% is used for education expenses. As a result, the township office only has an income of over a hundred yuan and cannot even open for business. The difficulty of autonomy is evident.

Anqing

The First Step in the Party and Government Organs' Handling of Disputes in the Education Community: The education community in Anhui Province has recently experienced a major dispute, involving a wide range and difficult to resolve. The cause of the dispute is the attack on education inspectors in the "Education New Publication" (a new publication of the Anhui education community). The Department of Education had previously sent Yang Zhongming and five others to study abroad. Yang and others took the money but did not go abroad. The "Education New Publication" first wrote articles urging them, then wrote articles scolding them. Cao Juesheng, the editor of the publication, then published advertisements questioning why Yang and others did not go abroad. Yang and others considered this an insult and sued Cao in court. Cao also gathered many people and sued Yang with the provincial government. Advertisements in the newspapers appeared repeatedly. The "Education New Publication" is Cao's stronghold, and the School Federation is Yang's protector. The conflict has become intense. The provincial party headquarters, believing that both sides are wrong, first submitted a request to the provincial government to cancel the provincial school federation, saying that it was organized without permission and violated the law. At the same time, it also rejected the registration of the "Education New Publication," saying that it incited student unrest. This is the first step in handling disputes in the education community. There is currently no definite news on how to proceed with the second step. Cao and Yang are currently evenly matched and at a standstill. A thorough resolution is expected soon.

Problems Arise with Anhui University School Buildings: Anhui Provincial University has been established for three years but still has no fixed school buildings. The agricultural school buildings at Wulimiao outside the East Gate are small and dilapidated and insufficient. Therefore, the school buildings of St. Paul's Middle School have been rented repeatedly, but have not been vacated. Now that St. Paul's Middle School has been restored, it has informed the provincial government, the Department of Education, and Anhui University that the lease will expire in February of next year, and the school buildings must be fully recovered and will not be re-leased. The school is currently trying to remedy the situation.

Important Education News

Ministries Jointly Submit Measures for Establishing Secondary Schools in Various Leagues and Banners of Mongolia

The Ministry of Education and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission have drafted an outline of measures for establishing secondary schools in various leagues and banners of Mongolia (listing more than a dozen areas, each to establish secondary schools, vocational schools, and rural normal schools. Two or three secondary schools should be fully established before the 26th year of the Republic and rural normal schools and vocational schools must be established first). The submission to the Executive Yuan states that the allocation of Mongolian and Tibetan education funds for the 20th year is: 90,000 yuan for the regular expenses of the National Mongolian and Tibetan School, 300,000 yuan for subsidies for secondary schools established in areas densely populated by Mongolians, Tibetans, and Xinjiang Hui people, 30,000 yuan for subsidies for Mongolian, Tibetan, and Xinjiang Hui students studying in secondary schools and above in the interior, 20,000 yuan for scholarships for those studying abroad, 30,000 yuan for printing textbooks suitable for Mongolian and Tibetan secondary and lower schools, 10,000 yuan for textbook and popular reading material translation awards, 10,000 yuan for academic investigation team subsidies, and 10,000 yuan for special expenses. The budget book has already been submitted separately for review. These funds are primarily intended to develop local education in Mongolia and Tibet. Once the allocation methods and budget are finalized, they should be actively implemented according to the Mongolian and Tibetan education implementation plan. However, the political organization and social conditions of Mongolia and Tibet are different from those of the interior. If separate, practical, and unified measures are not formulated, there is a risk of disputes or no one being responsible for planning once the funds are released. According to the original plan, the secondary schools established in various leagues and banners of Mongolia, except for the four special banners that are attached to nearby leagues and banners, will use the original administrative areas of each league and banner as the enrollment area. The schools are not all in one place and cannot all be located in the offices of the league and banner chiefs. If the league and banner chiefs are solely responsible for running the schools, the current actual situation suggests that it may not be done perfectly or may lead to neglect. If the officials of the banner where each school is located are responsible for running the schools, the school's interests may be exclusively for that banner, or other banners may not be responsible for sending students or sharing expenses. The central government's subsidies for these schools are limited. If the central government directly sends people to run the schools, there may be communication problems and more obstacles to progress. Furthermore, the existing educational foundation in various leagues and banners of Mongolia is uneven. Some have already established secondary schools, while others have not even established primary schools. All these practical situations should be planned in advance so that education in various leagues and banners of Mongolia can progress in an orderly and balanced manner. The ministry and commission have discussed in detail and unanimously agree to first draft a twelve-article outline of measures for establishing secondary schools in various leagues and banners of Mongolia, covering the nature, number, location, time limit, order of establishment, enrollment area, administrative organization methods and procedures, educational policy, and fundraising, with the goal of making clear and consistent progress without obstruction. Is this appropriate? A joint submission is made for review and approval for instruction and implementation.
