Local News Two

News of Disaster Relief for Victims

Italy Agrees to Allocate Boxer Indemnity Funds for Disaster Relief: Chairman Song of the National Government's Water Disaster Relief Committee announced that a contract has been signed with the Italian government to allocate US$200,000 from the Italian Boxer Indemnity funds for the purchase of disaster relief equipment and other materials. These equipment and materials will be purchased from Italy by the managers of the China-Italy Bank and the Italian Bank. The procurement contract will be negotiated and finalized by representatives appointed by the National Government and the Italian representatives. This allocation of Boxer Indemnity funds is considered a special measure of a charitable nature for disaster relief and should not be taken as a precedent for future allocations. Chairman Song expressed great satisfaction with the Italian government's concern for the disaster situation and its ready agreement to the National Government's proposal to use Boxer Indemnity funds for relief efforts. He also expressed deep appreciation for the efforts of the Italian Chargé d'Affaires in China, Count Ciano, in completing this matter. The Chinese side has appointed Mr. Wang Jingchun, who is currently handling matters related to the British Boxer Indemnity in London, as its representative to liaise with the Italian representative, Mr. Shexi, regarding the required equipment and materials. It is reported that inquiries have already been made to Italy to facilitate consideration and procurement.

Champagne Winner Donates 50,000 Yuan: The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief for Water Disasters in Various Provinces received the following donations yesterday: (1) Mr. Tang Baoshu, the first prize winner of the recent charity champagne draw, wrote to Mr. Xu Jingren, the standing committee member of the committee, stating that the winning ticket for the grand champagne draw was handled by Mr. Xu Wenliang, with the prize being equally divided among Xu Wenji, Huang Changji, Tang Guoji, Huang Yingji (Ms.), and Jisheng Hall, totaling five shares. Mr. Xu, with his charitable heart, requested that each of the five parties donate 10,000 yuan, totaling 50,000 yuan, for disaster relief. Enclosed with the letter was 50,000 yuan, hoping that the committee would accept it and distribute it to the affected areas, ensuring that the disaster victims receive tangible benefits, and not disappointing Mr. Xu's enthusiasm for relief. (2) Lawyer Yao Da donated 100 yuan himself and raised 230 yuan, totaling 330 yuan. (3) The Shanghai Bar Association continued to submit 230 yuan and two donation registers. (4) A telegram from Funing County (29th) stated that the county had established 18 porridge kitchens, with a large number of disaster victims, and had received 5,000 bags of flour, which had not yet arrived, leaving the victims in dire need of food. (5) A letter from Mr. Ye Yizhou stated: "Greetings to the standing committee members. During the peak of fundraising for the recent water disaster, the Northeast Incident suddenly occurred, shifting the nation's attention. Coupled with the extremely tight monetary situation, the committee's income plummeted, which is deeply regrettable. Many provinces are currently distributing relief, but due to the widespread disaster and limited funds, they are requesting additional allocations. Relief efforts in the disaster areas cannot be stopped. Furthermore, the commissioners of relief from various provinces are requesting to take over winter relief, work relief, and agricultural relief. The telegrams are flying in like snowflakes, and the reports are too tragic to bear. The floodwaters are gradually receding in various places, but the disaster victims, who fled for their lives during the floods, have been separated from their families. To this day, they do not know the whereabouts of their parents, siblings, wives, and children, and their reunion is uncertain. Even if they return home, their houses are gone, and the ruined wells and desolate walls present a scene of desolation. Moreover, they have no seeds left and are still exposed to the elements without clothing or shelter. They are at risk of freezing to death as the north wind howls and chills their bones, causing tears to fall. I, Yizhou, have no other hobbies in my life except smoking cigarettes. Deeply moved by the sight of the disaster, I am now saving my cigarette money for ten days, totaling three yuan, and submitting it to the committee to be distributed to the disaster areas. I know that this is just a drop in the bucket, but Shanghai is the largest commercial port in the country, with a population of no less than three million people. The city is extremely prosperous, with wealthy merchants, foreign firms, and prominent overseas Chinese. It is as if they are in heaven looking down on the disaster areas, which are like hell. I hope that the elders, brothers, sisters, and compatriots of this city will all have a kind heart and make a great wish to contribute their luxury goods or non-essential expenses for this winter, such as entertainment, gambling, food, pursuit, singing and dancing halls, movies, ballparks, and cosmetics for famous ladies and stars, each person reducing their entertainment once or buying two fewer items. The cost is not much, and the pain is limited. I propose that all citizens of the city make two wishes: to donate to this committee once within the next month, averaging three yuan per person. With a population of two million people in the city, this would generate an income of six million yuan, which can be used for winter relief, setting up porridge kitchens and warming centers, and providing cotton clothing and bedding. Small contributions make a large sum, and grains of sand build a tower. This is my humble wish." The Shanghai Anhui Water Disaster Relief Association, regarding the closure of the Shanghai Municipal Disaster Victim Reception Center, considers this matter to be of great importance and has sent separate letters to the National Government Relief Committee, the Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief in Various Provinces, the Relief Committee, the Chinese and Foreign Charity Association, the Red Cross Society, the Red Swastika Society, the Jisheng Association, and the Zhabei Charity Group, stating: "We are writing to you regarding the news reported recently that the Shanghai Municipal Disaster Victim Reception Center has been ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau to close at the end of November. We have also received a letter from the center stating that it has now stopped receiving disaster victims and that no more victims should be sent to the center. The disaster situation in the Jianghuai region is the most severe. The number of victims who have been submerged is countless, and those who have survived until now due to incomplete relief efforts continue to suffer. As the floodwaters gradually recede and transportation becomes more convenient, the number of people fleeing to Shanghai for their lives has actually doubled compared to before. They are supporting the old and carrying the young, appearing emaciated and haggard, wandering the streets and markets, unable to find help. Having been displaced for a long time, they will eventually starve and freeze to death. According to the reports from the six staff members stationed at the reception center by our association, including Mr. Zhu Runbin, every night, dozens or hundreds of disaster victims fleeing from the Yangtze River coast, such as Wuwei and other areas, as well as Jiangbei and Huaibei, arrive at the center, appealing for help at the door. However, they are refused admission and are forced to be dispersed by the police, leaving them exposed to the elements and their cries unanswered. Upon receiving this information, our association immediately dispatched Mr. E Runzhi by car late at night on the 25th of this month to negotiate repeatedly and strongly urge the center to take them in and provide them with porridge, which finally allowed them to settle down. However, they had no blankets to sleep on and were shivering with cold. Moreover, the Second Reception Center still has 40 to 50 empty rooms, and the 450 shi of rice donated by the Jiangbei rickshaw pullers' union is temporarily not lacking. Messrs. Zhu and E reported to Mr. Wang Yiting, Mr. Qu Wenliu, Mr. Wang Binyan, and other gentlemen at the Renji Hall and the Zhabei Charity Group, who all disapproved of the situation. The Jiangsu Charity Association immediately allocated 5,000 yuan, and other charitable groups continued to provide assistance, so there is no need to worry about food. However, the director of the center is strictly following orders and not completing the task of doing good, which is truly incomprehensible. Receiving disaster victims is essential for disaster relief. The center has already received more than 6,000 people, and more than 2,000 people have been sent away. There are also many people who have left the center voluntarily. Now, new people are arriving in Shanghai from various places, all seeking a way to make a living. Since a large number of them have already arrived, they should all be taken in. If the government is facing difficulties, it should consult with various charitable groups to discuss solutions. How can they be refused admission? If there is no proper resettlement, the hunger and cold of the disaster victims will affect local public order, and it would be unbearable for us to let them be left to die after seeking refuge. Therefore, we have sent Messrs. Zhu and E to your association with this letter to request a consultation on the proper way to receive and resettle the victims, saving lives and providing thorough relief, which would be a great act of merit. The Shanghai Anhui Water Disaster Relief Association."

Clothing Association Distributes a Large Batch of Relief Clothing: The Clothing and Bedding Aid Association at 207 Ximengdelan Road, Racecourse, has received over 35,000 pieces of clothing and bedding and over 500 quilts from various sectors since its establishment. Two Kidnappers Executed Yesterday

Wang Zhenshi Case: Zhu Xiangsheng

Deng Zhonghe Case: Weng Zisheng

Kidnapper Zhu Xiangsheng (also known as Zhu Amao), a native of Chuansha, 44 years old, colluded with accomplices on March 27th of this year to kidnap Dr. Wang Zhenshi from No. 2, Xinghe Lane, 411 Jing'an Temple Road, and hide him at No. 264, Xieping Lane, Beile Road. Later, Wang was redeemed with a huge sum of money. Subsequently, Chief Inspector Lu Liankui and Detective Wang Chengying of the General Inspectorate arrested Zhu and sent him to the First Special Court, which sentenced him to death. The sentence was approved by the Jiangsu Provincial Government for execution. Kidnapper Weng Zisheng (also known as Weng Azhi), a native of Ningbo, 33 years old, kidnapped Deng Zhonghe, the owner of the Daqing Cotton Cloth Store, on Ningbo Road on April 3rd of the previous year and took him to Pudong. Later, Chief Detective Wang Changgen and Su Changsheng arrested Weng and sent him to the former Provisional Court, which, after investigation, sentenced him to death. The sentence was approved by the Provincial Government for execution. Yesterday afternoon was the execution date. The police escorted the two criminals, Zhu and Weng, to the Third Criminal Court of the Special Court. Judge Cheng Shangfeng took the bench and asked the two criminals if they had any last words. Zhu stated, "Please send a letter to Xu Xiechang South Goods Store at the entrance of Caojia Road, Pudong, to be forwarded to my father, Wei Zhaoying, telling him that I died of illness so that he will not be too sad. If he has money, he can come to collect my body. If he doesn't have money, he can forget about it. Also, there were three yuan that were confiscated. Please ask the police to buy long ingots to burn for me so that I can use them in the underworld." Weng stated, "Please write a letter to my mother at No. 1, Jiaotong Lane, Qiujiang Road, telling her not to be sad. At that time, I was defrauded of more than 1,000 yuan by Yang Jitang while working at the Nisshin Company. Please ask my mother to go and get it back. Also, when I was arrested, many of my clothes and other items were confiscated. When I was in the Western Prison, I asked the head of the prison, who said that the police had not sent them. Please investigate." Judge Cheng Shangfeng then inquired with lawyer Zhang Tianyin of the police, who agreed to investigate with the police and report back. Judge Cheng then ordered the two criminals to be taken down. The guards put them in a car and drove to the Caohejing execution ground. Officials from the Local Court were dispatched to supervise the execution by firing squad.

Zhu Chengzhang Case: Kidnappers Sentenced to Death

Yuan Awei and Zhang Shiming Both Sentenced to Death

Chen Xing Acquitted and Released Immediately

Chief Detective Wang Changgen of the General Inspectorate of the General Patrol Room and Chief Detective (surname missing) of the Zhabei Patrol Room previously arrested three kidnappers: Yuan Awei (also known as Awei De Yuan Xiaomao), a native of Ningbo; Zhang Shiming (also known as Zhang Jinsheng Xiaojinsheng), a native of Suzhou; and Chen Xing, a native of Changzhou. It was found that Yuan and others kidnapped Zhu Chengzhang, the president of the National Goods Bank, at 9:00 AM on December 23rd of last year, and shot and killed Zhu, wounding Zhu's daughter Chengxiu and the nurse Deng Changcai. They also shot and killed Heersi, No. 247 of the Third Team of the Zhabei Patrol Room, and the Chinese assistant A'er near the New Company at 12:40 AM on March 4th of the previous year. They also kidnapped Lou Kenzai, the son of Lou Xunru, the president of the Quangong Bank, on Wenzhi Road at 9:00 AM on November 4th of the previous year. They also robbed 46,000 yuan of silver from the Four Banks' reserve warehouse in a small alley on Guangdong Road and Fuzhou Road at 2:15 PM on March 13th of last year. Lawyer Ru Baoyi, representing the patrol room, prosecuted them in the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court in accordance with Articles 1 and 2 of the Punishing Kidnapping Law and the crimes of robbery and murder under the Criminal Law. After several summons and interrogations, the case was concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Han, the chief of the Criminal Court, took the bench in the First Criminal Court and announced the verdict. The main text of the verdict stated that Yuan Awei was sentenced to life imprisonment for two counts of joint murder, Zhang Shiming was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for the crime of joint robbery with three or more people carrying weapons, and Yuan Awei and Chen Shiming were each sentenced to death for the crime of joint kidnapping for ransom, with the death penalty to be executed. Chen Xing was acquitted. Upon hearing the verdict, lawyer Ru of the patrol room rose and declared that he would waive the appeal for Chen Xing's acquittal and requested that he be released immediately. The court granted the request.

Tang is the Deputy Accountant of Guangxing Store

The Owner of the Store, Mr. Chen, Was Also Kidnapped

Tang Wenfu, a Cantonese man and the deputy accountant of Guangxing Store, which specializes in warehousing, located at No. 180, Xingye Lane, Miller Road, Hongkou, 22 years old, was suddenly kidnapped by bandits at around 8:45 AM yesterday morning. Where Did the Two Boys Come From?

Hidden in a Quilt, Suspicious Doubts

Claiming Mr. Lin is Just an Excuse

At around 4:00 PM yesterday, Chen Songshan and Li Fengqi, officers of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, were patrolling the river near the Ning-Shao Wharf at the Sixteenth Pier when they saw that the Ningxing steamboat was still moored. They immediately went aboard to inspect it. They found a woman in the cabin forcing a boy dressed in a Zhongshan suit to sleep under a quilt. The boy was crying and refused, sticking his head out from under the quilt. The woman forced him back under the quilt, but the boy still refused, sticking his head out. The officers found this very strange and immediately interrogated her about her background and asked who the boy under the quilt was. The woman said that the boy was her son. When they asked her what the boy's name was, the woman could not answer. At that moment, the officers noticed that something seemed to be bulging inside the quilt and moving. They became even more suspicious and immediately lifted the quilt, revealing another lively and lovely boy dressed in a cotton robe curled up on the bed. They questioned the woman again, asking what her relationship was with the boy. The woman claimed that he was her grandson. The officers observed that the two boys were both around three years old and did not resemble the woman. They suspected that they were not her children or grandchildren and that their backgrounds were unknown. They took the woman and the two boys to the team. During the preliminary interrogation by Director Xu, after questioning the woman repeatedly, she confessed that she was Ge Xu, 46 years old, from Suzhou, living on Hulong Street in Suzhou. The boy in the cotton robe, named Jin-er, was three years old this year. He was given to her by a Mr. Lin she knew at a hotel at the Zhangmenkou in Suzhou and asked to take him to Shanghai to transfer to a boat to Fujian. Mr. Lin promised to give her a reward of ten yuan. The boy in the Zhongshan suit was given to her by Mr. Lin in Shanghai, so she did not know his name. She said that she was confused for a moment and greedy for the small profit, so she did not ask Mr. Lin about the background of the two boys. She then began to weep, regretting what she had done. The officers observed that the clothes worn by the two boys were newly made and that they were innocent and naive. They suspected that they had been abducted by bandits, disguised, and trafficked to Fujian to be sold. They ordered a document to be prepared and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

Electricity Company's New Office Building

Moving in for Office Work on the Second of Next Month

The Shanghai Electric Power Company announced that it will be relocating all offices from the old site in the Public Works Department building to its newly built building at 95 Nanjing Road, near the corner of Jiangxi Road, on Monday, November 2nd. The new building began construction in 1930, but due to various delays in the construction project, it was unable to move in as scheduled. However, most of it is now ready, so it will be moved in immediately. The company hopes that customers will understand any inconvenience caused by this. All offices will be moved to the new location. As for the sample rooms in the Sassoon House, it will have to wait until the middle of next month, so the service to the public at that location will remain the same. The purpose of each floor of the new building is as follows: The first floor is for sample rooms and will be reported in detail later. All departments that were previously in the Sassoon House sample rooms and collection office and are related to the public will also be concentrated here to avoid inconvenience for customers. The second floor is dedicated to the customer accounting room and the company's preferred stock office, which is fully equipped for transactions with the public. The third floor is for the accounting room and material room. The fourth floor is for the power feed engineer's office. The fifth floor is for the deputy manager, chief engineer, secretary, and customer engineer's office. The motor rental department, archives, and communications room are also located on this floor. The sixth floor is for the president's office, vice president and general manager's office, board room, meeting room, and future expansion areas for various departments. Transportation between floors is facilitated by two new-style elevators that have never been seen in Shanghai. As for the company's telephone number, it will be changed to 11010 from the date of moving into the new building, which is easy to remember. The postal address will remain the old mailbox number 404.

Zhabei Rice Prices Falling

Recently, due to the arrival of new grains and the abundant supply, the rice prices in this port have fallen. In the Zhabei area, more than 40 rice boats arrived yesterday, and the market sales were sluggish. Therefore, the prices of various types of rice were more than three yuan lower per shi than the original limited price of seventeen yuan. The rice prices yesterday were recorded as follows: The highest quality old polished rice was fourteen yuan per shi, the next was thirteen yuan and four jiao, and the lowest was twelve yuan and five jiao. Old Tongbian glutinous rice was also fourteen yuan. The embossed was twelve yuan and nine jiao. The highest quality new japonica rice was fourteen yuan, the next was thirteen yuan, and the next was twelve yuan and four jiao. New Yangxian rice was thirteen yuan, the next was twelve yuan and four jiao. Port Xian rice was twelve yuan and four jiao, the next was ten yuan and six jiao. According to people in the rice industry, if the weather clears up, there will be more goods coming in from various places in the future, and the prices will have to fall again.

Tragedy of a Small Boat Colliding with a Rowboat

Seven People Drowned Together

At 6:15 PM the night before last, eight passengers boarded rowboat No. 150 from the Zhaofeng Road Wharf in Hongkou to cross to Pudong. When they arrived near the Xiaonanyang Wharf in Pudong, a small boat belonging to the Asia Company arrived from the Xinguang Wharf. Because it was dark and both sides had lights on, they were careless in identifying the direction, causing the bow of the small boat to crash into the rowboat. The rowboat could not withstand the impact and was overturned. All eight passengers and the boatman Ding Xilong and his wife fell into the water. The small boat quickly tried to rescue them, but only two passengers and the boatman Ding Xilong were rescued. Six passengers and Ding's wife drowned and disappeared. Although Ding was rescued, his face, hands, and feet were injured, but not seriously. Afterwards, Yang Wanying, the captain of the small boat, and Ding reported the incident to the Yangshupu Water Patrol Room. The captain, based on the statements of both parties, each with their own reasons, ordered them to stay in the patrol room overnight. Yesterday afternoon, detectives Hu Changqing and Shen Changshan escorted the plaintiff and defendant to the local court for investigation. The bodies of Ding's wife and the six passengers who died have not yet been found. It is likely that the families of the deceased passengers have not yet received the news of the tragedy, so they have not reported it to the patrol room. The patrol room detectives are currently investigating and sending people to search for the bodies.

Methods for Certifying National Products

To be handled by the National Products Exhibition Hall

Since the Shanghai Social Bureau's National Products Exhibition Hall was approved by the Municipal Government to handle the certification of national products, hundreds of manufacturers in the city have applied for certification. The hall has been dispatching personnel to various factories for detailed investigations, keeping them very busy. It is understood that, to facilitate the application procedures for manufacturers, an application form has been printed. Any applicant for registration and certification can obtain the form at the hall. It is also understood that the hall's standard methods for certifying national products are based entirely on the national product standards promulgated by the Ministry of Industry. Therefore, applicants for certification at the hall can have the hall forward their applications to the Ministry of Industry for the issuance of certificates. During this period of the boycott movement, the certification of national products is of great importance. A reporter from the Wuchen News Agency has specially obtained the certification regulations, the national product grade standards promulgated by the Ministry of Industry, and the products of various factories that have been certified by the hall, as follows:

Certification Methods: (1) Any manufacturer in the city who wishes to apply to this hall for certification that their products are indeed national products shall comply with these methods. (2) The applicant shall submit an application form, along with samples of the products for which certification is requested, together with drawings, specifications, and trademarks, three copies each, for review. (3) The application form shall specify the following items and be signed and sealed by the applicant or their agent: (1) Product name; (2) Trademark; (3) Producer; (4) Place of production; (5) Capital; (6) Factory or company name; (7) Raw materials; (8) Labor. (4) Each certificate is limited to one type of product. (5) Certification fees are temporarily waived; only a handling fee of two yuan per item is collected, to be submitted with the application. However, if the same manufacturer applies for certification for two or more products at the same time, the handling fee will only be charged once. (6) If, after on-site investigation by personnel from this hall, the products submitted for certification are found to meet the national product standards stipulated by the Ministry of Industry, a certificate will be issued according to the grade. (7) In case of any doubt, certification will be suspended, and the handling fee will not be refunded. However, if there are special reasons, the producer may apply for a re-examination. (8) All national products certified by this hall shall be entitled to the rights under various national product preferential treatment regulations in this city and may request to be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry for the issuance of national product certificates promulgated by the Ministry. (9) If there are any matters not covered in these methods, they may be revised at any time and reported to the competent authorities for filing with the Municipal Government. (10) These methods shall be implemented from the date they are submitted to the Social Bureau and forwarded to the Municipal Government for approval.

National Product Standards Promulgated by the Ministry of Industry

First Grade: Chinese Capital, Chinese Management, Entirely Domestic Raw Materials, Chinese Labor, Foreign Technicians

Second Grade: Chinese Capital, Chinese Management, Mostly Domestic Raw Materials, Chinese Labor, Foreign Technicians

Third Grade: Chinese Capital with Foreign Loans, Chinese Management, Entirely Domestic Raw Materials, Chinese Labor

Fourth Grade: Chinese Capital, Chinese Management, Mostly Foreign Raw Materials, Chinese Labor, Foreign Technicians

Fifth Grade: Chinese Capital with Foreign Loans, Chinese Management, Mostly Domestic Raw Materials, Chinese Labor, Foreign Technicians

Sixth Grade: Chinese Capital with Foreign Loans, Chinese Management, Mostly Foreign Raw Materials, Chinese Labor, Foreign Technicians

Worker Jin Shifa Still Denied Re-employment

Municipal Government to Arbitrate Conditions for Zhonghua Today

Municipal Government to Arbitrate Today: The Municipal Government Labor-Management Arbitration Committee is scheduled to arbitrate the Zhonghua Bookstore employees' terms of employment at 1:00 PM this afternoon. The Publishing Industry Labor Union has designated Yang Youren and Wang Wenhua as representatives to attend the arbitration meeting.

Recent News on Pilotage Examination

Foreigners Attempt to Protract Control

Organizing an Examination Committee

Our country's recovery of pilotage rights is in its preliminary stages, first by holding examinations and then establishing a management committee to gradually proceed. The Ministries of Finance, Communications, and Navy have drafted measures for the recovery of pilotage rights, which have been approved by the Executive Yuan. On one hand, preparations are being made for the examination, originally scheduled to be held in Shanghai on October 1st, but later postponed by one month due to insufficient time. Now, with the date of the examination approaching, the Shanghai Pilots' Association, having learned that the examination regulations stipulated by the central government allow foreigners to take the same exam, and that the organized pilotage management committee will be mostly composed of foreigners, meaning that the power to select pilots in the future will still be controlled by foreigners, which is far from the goal of recovering pilotage rights, submitted a report to the Ministry of Navy on the 12th of last month expressing their opposition. Now, they have submitted another report to the Examination Yuan, detailing the foreigners' conspiracy to control pilotage. The details of this matter are divided as follows:

Report to the Examination Yuan: The Shanghai Merchant Marine Masters Association's report to the Examination Yuan states, "Upon investigation, the foreigners' conspiracy to seize pilotage is entirely systematic, as can be seen in the report submitted to the Ministries of Finance, Navy, and Communications on June 27th of this year. We hereby present a summary: The foreigners want to continue to control and prolong the life of the South Mouth Pilots' Association, so the president of the association lobbied powerful foreigners to exert some kind of influence, implicitly forcing our country, under certain circumstances, to recognize the necessity of the foreigners' continued existence, or at least as a kind of exchange, and to use certain situations to give foreign pilots a stronger guarantee under our country's laws. They also spread various rumors, trying to distort the truth and confuse the public, even going so far as to attack, as seen in publications like the "Shipping Weekly," which often contain fallacies such as "Chinese pilots, even if established, can only pilot Chinese ships; foreign ships are led by foreign pilots," and claims that "Chinese pilots cause foreign ships to hesitate, affecting tax revenue," disregarding our country's sovereign rights and the abilities of our citizens. However, clever words can only deceive for a time, and will not withstand the facts. For example, in July of this year, foreign pilots at South Mouth threatened to strike, and after seven days of stalemate, what percentage of tax revenue was actually affected? Does the Customs have accurate statistics, or are the speakers just making unfounded statements? The speakers and listeners all have their own intentions, which should be specially noted by those in the know. Currently, the number of Chinese people serving as pilots in the South Mouth section is indeed small, but it should be known that seventy years ago, whether in the South Mouth section or in various ports in China, the pioneering founders of pilotage were all Chinese. Only because Hart deceived the Qing court and presented the management rights to foreigners, did they gradually seize them through cunning and coercion. This is truly a painful history for our Chinese people. Looking at more recent events, in 1928, a Chinese man named Li Gaochang served as a pilot in the South Mouth section and achieved excellent results. Unfortunately, he resigned due to illness. Li was succeeded by Lin Guojie, whose performance was also very good, which caused the foreigners to be wary. They incited foreign shipping companies to oppose him, but because Lin's skills were excellent and there was no excuse to be found, the opposition scheme turned into various slanders, falsely accusing our pilots, hoping to prolong their control. Even more despicable, our association member Yang Ying, when serving in the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, discovered that among the Western captains and crew members, some had no diplomas but pretended to have positions, and others had diplomas but were incompetent. He did his best to remove these people, and within six months, he employed more than 120 Chinese people. For four years, no accidents occurred. At the same time, the company's foreign employees, in November 1928, sank the "New Ji," in January 1929, sank the "New Hua," in July sank the "New Kangjiangqing," and in the upstream, rammed and sank the ferry "New Chang." The axle broke in 1928, and in March 1931, the "New Chang" sank. Each time an accident occurred, several to hundreds of Chinese people died, with no recourse. Chinese lives were as cheap as chickens. Today, competent Chinese crew members have no guarantee, and incompetent foreign crew members cannot be punished. Yet those foreigners still arrogantly claim that the level of Chinese pilots is immature. If their words are indeed true, how can they explain the superiority of the performance of Chinese crew members in the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company? Alas, the foreigners' manipulation of us Chinese people did not begin today, nor is it limited to the matter of pilotage alone. It has been going on for a long time. It is a pity that the Chinese people lack the skills, perseverance, and courage to respect and love themselves, and have been so trained as to take self-deprecation as humility and timidity as prudence, allowing the foreigners' upside-down and insulting remarks to flourish, anesthetizing people's hearts and weakening national spirit. Looking at the world today, how many can resist foreign invasion with real strength? Why not encourage and strive for progress in this area? I fear that in ten years, it will not only be a matter of the gains and losses of pilotage. Our association exposed the foreigners' conspiracy to control pilotage four months ago, and now their plans are being realized step by step. We urge you to uphold the spirit of fearlessness, to understand the crux of the matter, to safeguard the dignity of the examination, to give real benefits to the Chinese people, not to be confused by the foreigners' frivolous words, and not to be swayed by foreign forces, so that sovereign rights can be recovered and aggression can be broken."

Organizing Committee: With the pilot examination approaching, Examination Yuan Chairman Bu Yuan Chong specifically sent a letter to the Ministry of Navy, detailing that pilotage examinations should be prepared in advance, and that the Ministries of Finance, Navy, and Communications should jointly form a committee to thoroughly investigate the qualifications and academic requirements of pilotage candidates, as well as the areas of service, etc., so that there will be a basis for decision-making at the time of the examination. The letter also stated that foreigners who are allowed to take the exam should be lenient in their past but strict in their future, so that pilotage rights can be recovered after the expiration of the time limit in March 1934.

Japanese Fishing Boats Active Again in Shanghai

Hoping the Anti-Japanese Association will Pay Attention Promptly

Last year's incidents of Japanese fishing boats invading and fishing in Shanghai waters caused a stir for years and aroused the attention of Chinese people. Since the Customs implemented the new tariff, imported fresh fish are subject to an import tax of four and a half yuan per picul, with the original intention of protecting the domestic fishing industry. Limited by the tariff, Japanese fishing boats could not import. Later, they used Chinese merchants as traitors to transship on ice-fresh boats outside Wusongkou and import them as domestic products. However, with the cooperation of various fisheries organizations, the Navy's Coastal Defense Office and the Ministry of Industry's Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Administration dispatched ships to patrol outside Wusongkou, and the Shanghai Fisheries Guidance Station set up an office in Songkou to conduct inspections. Thus, the tricks of Japanese fishing boats were thwarted again. The Japanese, with their cunning plans, now transport the catches from Japanese fishing boats that invade and fish in our country's East China Sea and Yellow Sea to Dalian first, because Dalian Customs is still in the hands of the Japanese. Then, they transport them to Shanghai using Chinese ships, and no one can detect their fraud. As a result, Japanese fishing boats make huge profits, Chinese fish merchants make small profits, and the local Shanghai Chinese-owned fishing companies suffer losses. Because every time Japanese fish are imported from Dalian, the Shanghai fish market plummets, and Chinese fishing boats are greatly affected. Local fisheries organizations have reported that they are closely monitoring this matter. Please, Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, do not forget your own responsibility and investigate immediately, and notify the Shanghai Ice-Fresh Fish Industry Association to strictly order the fish shops at 16th Pier not to sell fish products imported from Dalian again. It is said that yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's ship Yushun and others imported two or three hundred barrels of small yellow croakers, eels, sharks, etc., causing panic among Chinese fishing boats. Please, Anti-Japanese Association, stop this quickly.

International Telegrams to be Reduced in Price Starting Tomorrow

At Nine Jiao in Chinese Currency per Gold Franc

Ten Thousand Jin Lost After Japanese Occupied Northeast Radio Station

International telegrams at the International Radio Station have always been calculated in gold francs, with each franc worth nine jiao and five fen in Chinese currency. Recently, the International Telecommunications Bureau received an order from the Ministry of Communications that, due to the depreciation of gold, each franc should be converted to nine jiao in Chinese currency, a reduction of five fen from before. The International Bureau has relayed this order to the radio stations to comply. Starting tomorrow, anyone sending telegrams will be charged five fen less per franc. Furthermore, according to Lu Guixiang, Director of the International Telecommunications Bureau, speaking to a reporter from the New Sound News Agency, since the Japanese army began invading the three northeastern provinces on the night of September 18th, the provinces of Liaoning and Jilin have fallen one after another, and the northeastern radio stations have been almost entirely occupied. Currently, only Harbin remains in the northeast. Therefore, from September 18th to today, the estimated loss of business for wireless telegraphs in the northeast will reach ten thousand jin. As for the loss of seized and destroyed equipment, the amount is even greater and almost incalculable.

Two Organizations to Hold Certification of National Products

The Shanghai Machine Joint Association replied to the Baoxing Factory's letter requesting instructions on how to hold certification of national products, "Regarding your respectful letter, we have already heard everything in the newspapers yesterday. Now we have received your letter, which states (the original letter can be found in the local news column of the Shen Bao on October 25th, omitted), etc. Upon investigation, this association has obtained permission from the government to organize a group of machine-made national product factories. It has been established for five years. We have done our best to develop and protect the interests of the association and its members. Although our capabilities are weak and we cannot fully satisfy the hopes of the association's workers and factories, we have done our best within our power. This time, with the outbreak of the Wanxian Incident and the occupation of the Northeast, all those with blood and energy are determined to cut off the enemy, either through boycotting or seeking alternative methods. The whole country is united and of one mind. In order to ensure the convenience of transportation for its members, this association first organized a national product certification advertisement, which was published in the Shen Bao and the Xin Bao for the first time on August 7th. Reduced-size leaflets were shipped with the goods. This was originally permitted by the government and allowed by law. If misunderstandings occur in various places, this association, as an organization of machine-made national products, will not stand idly by. If there are concerns in your letter, or even deliberate difficulties, and various destructions of national products, this is a public enemy of the factory and a reef of national products. Even if it is mistakenly detained for a time, it will certainly be clarified on another day. We are deeply grateful for your factory's care for this association. We are responding to the reasons stated in your letter. We hope you will take this into consideration." Addressed to Baoxing Mineral Powder Factory.

Minutes of the Board Meeting of the Shanghai Municipal Council

The Shanghai Municipal Council released the minutes of the board meeting held on the 28th, discussing various cases: (1) New building for the General Inspectorate, after the directors reviewed the engineering quarterly meeting minutes and discussed them, it was decided to build it on the west half of the vacant land at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Jiangxi Road, along the north side of Fuzhou Road, and to sell the remaining land, and to allocate a strip of open space on the west side to the American Club to purchase. In addition, it was also agreed in principle that if a new city hall is to be built in the future, it will be built on the existing site of the Municipal Council, without seeking another location. (2) The French Municipal Council notified that it intends to increase the bicycle registration fee from three yuan to four yuan starting next year, and asked if the Municipal Council is prepared to take consistent action. After discussion, it was considered that the purpose of bicycle registration was to facilitate police management and not for tax revenue. It was increased once last year, and if it is increased again next year, some people may find it difficult. Therefore, it was decided to notify the French Municipal Council that it has no intention to increase the fee. (3) Health Commissioner Dr. Marsh resigned, and Dr. Murray was appointed as his successor. (4) Due to overcrowding on public buses, it was decided that the Transportation and Public Utilities Committees would hold a joint meeting to discuss remedies. (5) Director Bland will leave Shanghai on November 10th and requested to resign immediately. The Director-General, on behalf of the entire board, expressed his regrets to Bland and wished him well in the future. (6) Someone contacted the bureau to ask if it would be willing to buy the Jiangbin Kaufman General Association property and open it as a park. It was considered that the land is located outside the concession and must be considered in cooperation with the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Report on Children's Cases by the Child Welfare Association

Total of 1,645 Cases in the Nineteenth Year

1,007 Cases Already Reached in the First Six Months of This Year

The Chinese Child Welfare Association, in order to thoroughly seek child protection and reduce social evils, specially collects information on child cases from newspapers, whether factual or rumored. This is done to accumulate daily, monthly, quarterly, and annual quantities, to investigate and compare the causes and effects based on temporality, locality, economic relations, customs relations, status, and gender, and to analyze and summarize them to create statistics and charts. Last year, from the beginning of January to the end of December, there were a total of 1,645 cases, averaging about 137 cases per month and slightly less than five cases per day. Lost children accounted for more than one-third, abducted children for more than one-tenth, kidnapped children for more than six percent, and children run over by vehicles, girls raped, and abandoned children each accounted for about four percent. There were even three cases of children being buried alive, two of children being boiled, and six of boys being sodomized. The association's statistics for the twentieth year, covering the six months from January to the end of June, have already reached 1,007 cases, an increase of slightly less than 200 cases compared to the same period last year. Lost children totaled 459, and abducted children totaled 156, both figures being similar to the total numbers for each category last year. Other cases included seven cases of abused maids, sixteen cases of apprentices suffering harm, eighteen cases of kidnapped children, three cases of women selling fetuses, thirty-four cases of girls being raped, two cases of child marriages, forty-two cases of children run over by vehicles, two cases of disputes over children, four cases of child suicides, four cases of abused adopted daughters-in-law, five cases of children forced into prostitution, one hundred and eleven cases of children being drowned, four cases of abandoned infant corpses, nine cases of child criminals, two cases of pregnant women being hit, two cases of children buried alive, twenty-eight cases of children burned to death, seven cases of abandoned children, four cases of boys being sodomized, twenty-six cases of children crushed to death by collapsing houses, three cases of parents killing their children, and fifty-nine cases of unclassified incidents. Although the association feels that it has exhausted all sources in collecting information and has strived for accuracy in its statistics, the number of cases that are actually lost, unheard of, concealed, or hidden is far more than this. However, the association's purpose is not in the quantity, but in the classification; not in the facts, but in the research; and not in the records, but in the publicity.

Reader's Letters

Letter from Fuliang Lin: Suicide is Not Loving the Country (Insufficient)

Recently, I saw in your newspaper that a few patriotic compatriots, out of anger and concern for the country in the face of Japanese aggression, have resorted to suicide. Their patriotic zeal is certainly commendable, but I do not approve of their actions. Suicide is the most cowardly expression of mankind. I consider people who commit suicide to be foolish at best. For example, in this case of committing suicide out of worry for the country and anger at Japan, I ask: after death, can you revive China? I believe that dying to love the country is not as good as living to save the country. Some say that suicide can arouse the patriotic fervor of the people, but I don't think so. The fervor of the people in resisting Japan depends entirely on the actual gains that the invading Japanese give us and the honest propaganda of the educated class. Even if you want to express your personal intensity and awaken the people, you can make enlarged publicity writings, you can cut off your finger and write a blood letter, why do you need to commit suicide lightly? If 400 million compatriots all commit suicide one by one, then the Republic of China will perish by itself. Some say that suicide is a positive expression of resisting Japan and saving the country, but that is even more wrong. If you want to actively die for China, you can petition the government to go to the front line to fight the Japanese bandits. Even death would be a happy one, at least more glorious, and it would also shock the Japanese's view of the Chinese national character. In short, I believe that in this critical period of resisting Japan, we should all do our best to engage in the movement of resisting Japan and saving the country, such as students working hard to publicize the return to double the effort to study, as a fundamental plan to save the country, or joining the volunteer army, the people's absolute boycott of Japanese goods, the people's absolute economic severance with Japan, the government's absolute non-compromise with the military, and the politicians' quick search for a livelihood, do not be political moths, and even more absolutely do not do traitorous acts... Then, the Republic of China, with thousands of years of history, will definitely not be burned down overnight. Patriotic compatriots, while we resist the bandits from outside, we must also strictly guard against the thieves inside the house!

Letters Received

To the Editor: In the October 28th issue of your newspaper, in the "Local News" section, it was reported that a freight train collided with the 10th passenger train on the Beijing-Shanghai line at Zhenru Xiyangqi, confirming that the 207th freight train did not reduce its speed when entering the station, causing it to rush out of the switch and reach the outer Yangqi, colliding with the 10th passenger train from Beijing. The location of the accident was originally at the station's Yangqi, which is a major responsibility for the responsible officers of this railway. According to the original report, the entire responsibility would be borne by me. The Ministry of Railways is in the capital, and the Management Bureau is in Shanghai, both nearby, making the matter very important to my position and status. Fortunately, the stationmaster of Zhenru Station admitted his fault. I hope that your reporter will re-inquire and publish the true situation. I am making this statement and requesting a correction in the "Letters to the Editor" column. With best regards to the editorial staff of the Local News section of Shenbao. From Lin Gangrui, train conductor of the 207th freight train. October 29th.

To the Editor: I was shocked to read in your newspaper today about the hiring of foreign sailors by Chinese shipping companies in Shanghai. Regarding the Haiphong Company's Jing Shun vessel's replacement of the chief officer, first mate, second mate, and helmsman on the 17th of this month, member He Shengcai reported to our association and requested our assistance in finding a replacement. As a united organization of Chinese marine engineers, we should provide protection. We sent a letter to the company recommending He Shengcai as the new helmsman. On the 27th, member Huang Duncai came to the association and forced us to send a letter. We had already made arrangements and could not send another letter. Moreover, He Shengcai and Cai Xingyi were registered earlier than Huang Duncai in the unemployment registration list. According to our association's regulations, unemployment registrations are processed in order and cannot be disrupted. Chen Rongsheng is not a member of our association and did not register. Huang Duncai and Chen Rongsheng campaigned privately. Our association is following the regulations, so there is nothing improper. The statement that Huang et al. were not allowed to serve as the first or second mate, and that the association had to send someone to fill the position, while Huang and Chen claimed that they were appointed by Haiphong and approved by the Maritime Administration, and that both sides refused to yield, and the engine room was even attempting to resolve the matter by force, is completely untrue. Our association is a general organization of marine engineers and should bear the responsibility. If the person who posted the notice has any objections, they should come to the association directly and not conspire to incite others. I am writing this letter to request a quick correction. I hope you will not see it as impolite. To the Chief Editor of Shenbao. Chinese Marine Engineers Association. October 30th.

Youth Garden

A Fiery Autumn Morning

— Luo Mang

In a daze, I pulled back the quilt. Silvery-white dawn streamed in from the window, carrying a brisk chill. My body shivered, and my mind cleared up.

I threw off the warm covers, got dressed, and heard the wind howling outside. This was an autumn morning.

I walked to the window and looked out at the vast parade ground, where many people had already gathered. At that moment, the shrill sound of a whistle pierced the air. He rushed out of the dormitory and ran towards the parade ground.

The air was bone-chillingly cold, and the students looked a little shrunken with the cold, their lips slightly blue. He reached out and picked up a wooden rifle. A gust of wind blew past, and goosebumps broke out all over his body. However, what was the cold to be afraid of? He had a fiery heart. No matter how cold it was outside, the colder it was, the more fiery and fervent it became inside him.

The instructor shouted the commands loudly.

His fervent heart beat wildly inside him. All of his blood vessels were powerfully stretched. His whole body seemed to contain boundless strength, ready to burst forth at any moment. He opened his mouth and exhaled bursts of hot air, as if to turn this cold surroundings into a fiery heat.

He stood at attention, his feet straight, all the strength of his body pouring down, flowing into his heels, into his toes. There was no more room for expansion below, as if he wanted to smash through the earth's crust.

The wind whipped the trees, causing them to rustle. Leaves fell from the branches and landed on the ground. The grass quivered. The withered branches, those gnarled, skeletal branches, were like the claws of the enemy, dancing before his eyes, about to pounce on him. He grabbed the wooden rifle with hatred, his chest filled with hot blood, as if he had to kill them all if they came any closer. His fingers were numb with the cold. However, he had a fiery heart. Could the cold make him retreat?

The instructor shouted the commands loudly.

Thick clouds covered the entire sky. The sun had lost its light and heat, making the surroundings even more gloomy and desolate. However, on this vast parade ground, these people on the parade ground had their own light and their own heat. They would use their light and heat to break through this surrounding gloom and desolation, and paint a vibrant scene.

They shouldered their rifles, they aimed. He pointed his rifle at a distant telephone pole, as if that telephone pole was the enemy. Sparks flew from his eyes. He wished he could go forward and pierce the enemy's chest with a bayonet, crush the enemy's heart and guts, wash away the shame of the motherland with the enemy's blood, and extinguish the fire in his heart. If the rifle in his hand was not a fake, then he would let bullets fly, killing the enemy one after another without leaving a single one.

They practiced charging.

He looked back at his comrades – his classmates, the citizens of the Republic of China. Each face shone with the light of revenge, each heart was fanned by the flames of killing the enemy. He thought in his heart, "Comrades, let us all charge forward, snatching back our existence, our happiness, and our glory from the hands of the enemy. We cannot let anything be lost. At the very least, we must pile up white bones into a tall fortress, and let red blood flow into a deep moat to block the enemy's advance. We cannot let anything be lost!"

The row of low trees in front seemed to be the enemy's position. The swaying branches seemed to be the enemies eager to move. "Comrades, let us charge over, trampling the enemy's camp into flat ground. We forget ourselves, forget everything, charge over, charge over, snatching back the glory of the motherland from the hands of the enemy!" Waves of blood surged high, mixing with the shouts of killing that broke the silence, like a tide, overflowing towards the enemy's position.

The instructor shouted the commands loudly.

Dust of the Road

— Tou Zhen

She arrived at my house with that plump baby in her arms, just as the pale yellow sunlight was beginning to illuminate the earth. I was holding the newspaper that had just been delivered, staring at it with intense eyes. Startling words were clearly imprinted on my eyes, one by one. As I read line by line, hot blood boiled. Her sudden arrival interrupted the impression the newspaper had given me, and I couldn't help but look at her in surprise.

It hadn't been ten days since she'd come to Shanghai from Guangzhou, and from Shanghai to Nanjing. I knew she was arranging the newly rented house in Nanjing.

"Rong, are you here in Shanghai for fun? I welcome you," I asked her in a typical Shanghai greeting, while offering her a seat.

"Did you arrive today?" I continued to ask.

"No," she replied as she sat down.

"I arrived last night at 5:00. I'm staying in an apartment. I didn't come to play, I came..." She hesitated, "He insisted I come, because their—their colleagues' families—have all come to Shanghai."

I immediately knew the reason she came. She was probably afraid that something similar to what happened in the three northeastern provinces would happen in Nanjing, so she braved the hardship of bringing her baby, who was less than a year old, to Shanghai and staying alone in an apartment. My house was in Nanshi, a dangerous area, so of course she didn't want to stay there. I didn't want to leave her either.

She didn't stay in the hotel for ten days, only seven days—a week—she wanted to go back. She couldn't stand the noise every night, especially the constant sound of mahjong tiles clacking, which never seemed to stop, constantly startling the baby in her arms and making it cry. She couldn't stand it anymore, so on the morning of the eighth day, she took the 9:30 express train back to Nanjing. Nanjing was still the same as before, and she was just pitifully caught in the dust of the road.

Page 20

Her Letter

— Qingzhi

Here is a letter from a friend of mine. I feel it is filled with the common pain and troubles of modern young women. I have specially copied it out, hoping that the readers can offer a solution.

Qingzhi

I originally didn’t want to write you such a letter, but there’s no way. My stomach feels like it’s about to burst. This bellyful of complaints or grievances is overflowing. How can I not find a way to let it out? If you cannot sympathize with me and get angry at me, then I can only ask you to forgive me for the sake of our friendship.

This morning, I wrote letters to several friends with great enthusiasm, making a bellyful of complaints that I couldn’t contain. As the old saying goes, "Think thrice before you act." Yes, especially for a chatterbox like me, complaining excessively can get you shot. I am unworthy of doing such a thing as complaining recently. Saving a few copper coins on postage to buy food can make my stomach feel better for a while. I will no longer bother with this letter-writing business. Let any thoughts or theories be expressed in dreams.

My heart is now filled with unspeakable sadness. Yesterday, I received a letter from my mother, showing how much she cares for me. The road is so far, and she is so old, yet she wants to come and see me because of my poor situation. My heart is truly uneasy. Alas, the elders only hope that I can create happiness for myself. Alas, powerless as I am, I am going to disappoint her wish. How could I not want to seek a little happiness for myself? But it is as difficult as walking from the sea to an island. I have failed her hopes, only causing her to worry about my life. I am truly sorry for her. My heart is constantly repenting to her. I, who am burdening her so much, wish she would remember my sins and be able to cast me aside from her loving embrace and forget me. That would make me feel better. But a mother's heart, her thoughts are not as simple as I say.

I want to abandon my mother's love to seek human sympathy and understanding, but in this world, where is there sympathy? Who can understand me? In this society, it is filled with only scolding, ridicule, cold stares, jealousy, and resentment. All sins are behaviors between you and me, but don't say I am exaggerating. In reality, we are still begging for pity and seeking sympathy. We are each other's only ray of light behind the black curtain in broad daylight. Perhaps the only thing is a little mutual self-interest.

Of course, love can intoxicate us, but, Qingzhi, do you know? Love, like the rays of the sun, makes you unfathomable. It is constantly obscured by dark clouds, and only for a few minutes can it shine on you. These few minutes of its power will wither your precious youth. At this time, don't examine it too closely, as too close an examination will make you feel there is no room for survival.

Dream on. In dreams, you can find a lover's embrace, that passionate kiss, a heart beating for you. It is entirely yours. It is not subject to any conditions, nor is it driven by any self-interest. Break through your iron shoes and sacrifice everything to find your lover. Friend, it is carefree and sound asleep in your dreams. Seek my happiness in dreams. Ah, are you busy pursuing happiness? Happiness is so abstract, so empty. Be as busy as you can, until a pile of yellow earth covers you completely, leaving nothing untouched.

Friend, how could you know my current situation? I will tell you and it will shock you. Because of a physical condition unsuitable for childbearing, I am at a certain hospital on Shanhaiguan Road in Shanghai... In my current environment, I am desperately poor. How can I afford to spend more money to pay respects to those so-called PhD doctors? I have been bedridden for over a month. Randomly seeking doctors is like knocking on the gates of hell, especially for poor people seeking doctors. Asking for their sympathy is like bargaining with ghosts. Chinese Western doctors are as cruel as imperialism. Naturally, seeking [doctors] is not opposed under this monetary system, where there is no pay without work. But the Western doctors who are profit-mongering imperialists are exploiting [patients] a bit too excessively. I am still sick, for over a month now. Because the surgery was not done well, I may have to suffer from uterine disease in the future. These sufferings are the result of me, a poor wretch, pursuing love and happiness in this unsuitable environment.

Although my own situation is so bad, I still want to act as a mediator when I see the two of you quarreling. Friend, take it easy. Pain is unavoidable in life. Changes in love can sometimes make you feel very sweet, and sometimes they can make you feel very painful. Things like love, marriage, the pains of life, and the period from childhood to adulthood that must be unconsciously passed through, are just as natural. Don't think that life is always happy. We receive a seed of suffering from the time we are in the womb. This suffering shares our life and death, and no one can escape it. Friend, be optimistic. Quarrels between two lovers are unavoidable. There is nothing worth suffering about. If you want to suffer over these small things, then you are really too foolish. Finally, I wish you less idealism, more practical effort, to reduce mental suffering. Your friend, Jianfei, October 23rd.
